text-align: justify; text-indent: -27.0pt; mso-list: l4 level1 lfo2;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">(v)<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">          </span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">There must be a chain of evidence so complete as not to leave any reasonable ground for the conclusion consistent with the innocence of the accused and must show that in all human probability the act must have been done by the accused.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 9.0pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 4.5pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo4;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">33.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">The circumstances, which, the prosecution has tried to establish in this case, are that there was previous day quarrel between the appellants and the victim and, on the next morning, dead body of the victim was recovered and the appellants were not found in their house. As to prove the case, by circumstantial evidence, well settled principle is that the circumstances from which the conclusion of guilt is to be drawn should be fully established and not ‘may be’ established. There is not only a grammatical but a legal distinction between ‘may be proved’ and ‘must be or should be proved’. There must be a chain of evidence so complete as not to leave any reasonable ground for the conclusion consistent with the innocence of the accused and must show that in all human probability the offence must have been done by the accused. The circumstances should be closely scrutinized and the same must be cogent, succinct, reliable and must be of a such a character as to exclude all possibility of the accused being innocent and there should be no weak links, every weak link being a ground of reasonable suspicion, always calling for an acquittal. Great care must be taken in evaluating circumstantial evidence and if the evidence relied on is reasonably capable of two inferences, the one in favour of the accused must be accepted. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 4.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 4.5pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo4;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">34.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Keeping in mind the views expressed above, let us examine the evidence adduced by the prosecution in this regard. From the testimonies of P.W.1 and P.W.14 it appears that before lodging formal FIR at about 3.15 on 17.07.1994 the P.W.1 went to Demra Police Station and informed the police about the occurrence and pursuant to that information the Officer-in-Charge of the Police Station directed P.W.14 to visit to the place of occurrence and, accordingly, P.W.14 S.I. Enamul Monwar rushed to the place of occurrence at about 10.30 a.m. He prepared inquest report of the deadbody of the victim. From the evidence of P.W.3 Abul Bashar it appears that the accused persons absconded before lodging FIR. He</span> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">said,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> “</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyMJ; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">wKšÍy Bmªvwdj, AvjgMxi, Avey Zv‡ni, Avwgbyj nK, Lyiwk`v †eMg I kvgmyb bvnvi‡K †`wL bv Ges Zvnviv evox nB‡Z cvjvBqv wMqv‡Q †`wL‡Z cvB| Bnvi ci Avgvi evev GB  gvgjvi GRvnvi `v‡qi  K‡i| </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">” </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">In FIR P.W.1 stated,</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> “</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: SutonnyMJ; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Avgvi †g‡q‡K †K ev Kvnviv gvwiqv Mv‡Q SzjvBqv ivwLqv‡Q Zvnv mwVK Abygvb Kwiqv AvBbvbyM e¨e¯nv wb‡Z gwR© nq|</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Courier New'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">” </span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">That is, till 3.15 p.m. at the time of lodging F.I.R. P.W.1 did not suspect the convicts and he also did not disclose in the FIR that the accused persons absconded subsequent after the occurrence. Even in his evidence he did not say anything about the story of appellants’ alleged abscondence. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 4.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 4.5pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo4;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">35.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">It is well known that different persons are differently constituted, and that some accused persons, though innocent, deliberately abscond rather face the ordinal of a criminal case. Even an innocent man may feel panicky and try to evade arrest when wrongly suspected of a grave crime. Absconding by itself need not necessarily lead to an inference of culpable mind against all the absconders. Absconding by itself is not conclusive either of guilt of a guilty conscience because the person may abscond on account of fear of being involved in the offence or for any other allied reason. </span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 4.5pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo4;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">36.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">In the case of Raghubir Singh V. State of U.P. reported in (1972)III SCC 79 it was observed that the act of absconding, even if proved, is normally considered a somewhat weak link in the chain of circumstances utilized for establishing the guilt of the accused. Moreover, the alleged facts of absconding was not put to the appellants is their examination under section 342 of the Code of Criminal Procedure so as to enable them to offer explanation.</span></p><p class="MsoListParagraph"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 4.5pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo4;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">37.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Probability of two views are possible in this case. The courts below convicted the accused (1)Israfil, (2)Abu Taher, (3)Alamgir, (4)Aminul Haque (5)Khorshida Begum and C(6)Shamsun Naher assuming that all of them, forming unlawful assembly with a common object to kill the victim, went to the place of occurrence and had killed the victim but we do not find any evidence either circumstantial or direct. There is no answer to the question as to who went to the place of occurrance and what was their actual number? All the members of the same family have been convicted relying only on presumption, surmises and conjectures. It is the cardinal principle of criminal jurisprudence that a case can be said to be proved only when there is certain and explicit evidence and no person can be convicted on pure on moral conviction. Another golden thread which runs through the web of the administration of justice in criminal cases is that if two views are possible on the evidence adduced in the case, one pointing to the guilt of the accused and other to his innocence, the view which favourable to the accused should be adopted. This principle has a special relevance in cases wherein the guilt of the accused is sought to be established by circumstantial evidence. On consideration of the evidence and the circumstances referred to above, we are satisfied that this is a case in which the circumstantial evidence did not prove the case against accused conclusively and unerringly, and at any rate two reasonable views are possible.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 4.5pt; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 4.5pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo4;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">38.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Moreover, in absence of prove of the ingredients of common object, the courts below committed error of law in convicting the appellants and others under sections 302/149 of the Penal Code. To secure conviction with the aid of section 149 of the Penal Code an overt act on the part of a member of unlawful assembly is </span></p><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_November_19(2)/Issue__November_19__Cr.%20A.%2003%20of%2010__Muhammad%20Imman%20Ali_J___AD___2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><em><u><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB;">CRIMINAL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>APPEAL<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>NO.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>03<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>OF<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>2010</span></u></em></strong></a><u> </u><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 9.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.2pt; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold;">(From the judgement and order dated 9<sup>th</sup> of August, 2007 passed by the High Court Division in Criminal Appeal No.351 of 2000)</span></p></div></div><p> </p></div></div>
810	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Anjuman Ara Begum Vs.  Friends Club and others.  </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Civil Revision No. 2740 of 2018  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Soumendra Sarker, J</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Probir Neogi, Senior Advocate with Mr. Md. Sumon Ali, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Anjuman Ara Begum  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Friends Club, Alamin Market, Gonestola, Dinajpur and others.</p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Premises Rent </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(CIVIL REVISIONAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Soumendra Sarker<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">, J</strong></span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">22.07.2019</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 55.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center;
