line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_November_19(2)/Issue%20__November__19(2)__C.R%20_2740%20of%2018_Soumendra%20Sarker,%20J.__1.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p></td><td style="width: 261.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Anjuman Ara Begum </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Plaintiff-Petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Friends Club, Alamin Market, Gonestola, Dinajpur and others.</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Defendant-Opposite Parties</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; color: white; mso-color-alt: windowtext;">Premises Rent Control Act (III of 1991)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 18</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The landlord is empowered to evict the tenant, when it is established that the tenant is a habitual defaulter in payment of rents and the landlord has basic need of the suit premises.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>.....(9)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Small Cause Courts Act (IX of 1887)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Sections 15 and 23</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Sections 15 and 23 of the Small Cause Courts Act does not confer any jurisdiction to the court in a S.C.C suit to enter into the question of title in respect of the suit premises, except incidentally or to set aside the decree passed in a civil court.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                     </span>...(12)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Order 1, Rule 10</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Where the co-shares are in possession of the suit premises, their application can be entertained under the ambit of Order 1 rule 10 of the Code of Civil Procedure but in the instant case it is not the case of the applicants that they are in possession of the suit premises along with the defendant Nos. 1 and 2. The impugned order No.58 dated 15.07.2018 passed by the learned Senior Assistant Judge, Sadar, Dinajpur in SCC Suit No.01 of 2010 allowing the application for addition of party is hereby set aside.<span style="mso-tab-count: 2;">               </span>...........(14 and 16)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Additional Deputy Commissioner (Revenue) and Assistant Custodian, Vested Property, Barisal –vs- Md. Mozammel Haque and another 16 BLD (AD) 237, 1981 BLD (AD) 128, Noor Mohammad-vs-Md. Noor Hossain and another 56 DLR 53, 2 MLR (AD) 357, 32 DLR (AD) 170 ref.</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Probir Neogi, Senior Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Md. Sumon Ali, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the petitioner</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. A.H.M Mushfiqur Rahman, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the Opposite Parties</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Soumendra Sarker</span></u></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Rule issued calling upon the opposite parties to show cause as to why the order No.58 dated 15.07.2018 passed by the learned Senior Assistant Judge, Sadar, Dinajpur in Small Causes Case No.01 of 2010 allowing the application for addition of party should not be set aside and/or such other order or further order or orders passed as to this court may seem fit and proper. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts giving rise to the issuance of the Rule in a nutshell can be stated thus: The present petitioner as plaintiff instituted the original Small Cause Courts Suit No.01 of 2010 in the Court of learned Senior Assistant Judge, Sadar, Dinajpur against the defendant-opposite parties for ejectment of tenants from the suit shop, contending inter alia that, the suit property originally belonged to one Md. Shahid Ali. The defendants are the President and Secretary of a Club namely ‘Friends Club’ and the defendants were the tenants under the landlord Shahid Ali. After the death of Shahid Ali his wife Firoza Begum and three sons namely, Md. Mirajul Islam, Md. Sirajul Islam, Md. Ferojul Islam and daughter Mst. Ifthesham Ali become the legal heirs of Md. Shahid Ali and the defendants were continuing their tenancy as monthly ejectable tenants under the aforesaid heirs of Shahid Ali. The monthly rent of the suit shop was fixed at Tk.1,000/- (one thousand). Subsequently, the plaintiff to the original suit purchased the land from the heirs of Shahid Ali by registered sub-kabala dated 20.11.2006 at a consideration of Tk.15,00,000/- (Fifteen lac). After purchasing the suit property while the defendants stopped in paying the rent in favour of the plaintiff, the plaintiff served a legal notice to the defendants to pay the rents in favour of her, on 02.03.2007, but the defendants did not pay the rent. Thereafter, the plaintiff served a notice under section 106 of the Transfer of Property Act, on 03.11.2009 and by this notice the plaintiff has terminated the tenancy with the defendants and asked the defendants to deliver vacant possession of the suit premises in favour of the plaintiff. The defendants received the notice by putting their signatures in the acknowledgment card on 08.11.2009. The further case of the plaintiff is such that the defendants out of ill-motive without payment of the rents to the plaintiff after filing a House Rent Control Case No.17 of 2007 depositing the rents to the court. The suit shop is badly required for the <em>bonafide</em> purpose of the plaintiff to construct a multistoried building thereon. During pendency of the original suit the defendants after making their appearance contested the suit by filing a written statement and at this stage the present opposite parties No.3-7 filed an application for addition of party under Order I rule 10 of the Code of Civil Procedure, alleging that the suit shop is the ancestral property of the applicant’s predecessor Wahida Begum, who was the sister of Md. Shahid Ali. Shahid Ali was possessing the property in <em>ejmali</em> with the predecessor of the applicants and thereafter died leaving behind three sons, one wife and one daughter. For getting a separate saham in the ejmali property, Wahida Begum filed a Partition Suit being No.192 of 2003 in the Court of learned Senior Assistant Judge, Sadar, Dinajpur, which is pending for disposal. The further case of the applicants is such that the sub-kabala deed of the plaintiff dated 20.11.2006 is illegal, inoperative and not binding upon the predecessor of the applicants Wahida Begum and challenging the said deed the successors of Wahida Begum i.e. the applicants filed an Other Class Suit No.105 of 2008 in the Court of learned Joint District Judge, 1<sup>st</sup> Court, Dinajpur, which is also pending for disposal. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned trial court by its order dated 15.07.2018 allowed the application for addition of party and being aggrieved by and dissatisfied with the impugned order the plaintiff as petitioner has preferred this civil revision under section 25 of the Small Cause Courts Act, 1887 and obtained the Rule with an interim order of stay.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">During hearing of the Rule, Mr. Probir Neogi, the learned Advocate appeared on behalf of the petitioner while Mr. A.H.M Mushfiqur Rahman, the learned Advocate appeared on behalf of the added defendant-opposite parties No.3-7.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the petitioner submits that the learned trial court in allowing the application for addition of party committed illegality. The learned Advocate further submits that the learned trial court failed to appreciate that the suit was filed by the owner of the suit premises for ejectment of tenants and the matter of adjudication in the instant suit is as to whether the relationship between the plaintiff and the defendants are landlord and tenants and as such the question of title to the suit premises is not relevant and not a matter of adjudication and as such the added defendants are not necessary parties or proper parties to the suit. The learned Advocate also submits that the decision cited by the learned trial court is not applicable in the instant suit due to distinguishable facts and feature of the case and the defendants after filing a rent control case have already recognized the plaintiff as owner to the suit premises, but the learned trial court in allowing the application for addition of party committed an error in law resulting in an error in the decision occasioning failure of justice. The learned Advocate in support of his submission referred some decisions of our Apex Court reported in 16 BLD(AD) 237, 1981 BLD (AD)128 and a decision of this Court reported in 56 DLR 53.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">As against the aforesaid submission of the learned Advocate for the petitioner, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the added opposite parties opposing the Rule controverted the argument advanced from the side of the petitioner and submits that, the learned trial Court during passing the impugned order dated 15.07.2018 in Small Causes Case No.01 of 2010 committed no illegality or irregularity. The learned Advocate further submits that the predecessor of the applicants is a co-sharer in the suit property with the vendor’s predecessor of the plaintiff Md. Shahid Ali. The learned court below rightly apprised the decision reported in 2 MLR(AD)357 and thereafter, allowed the application for addition of parties. The learned Advocate also submits that the opposite party’s predecessor-in-interest Wahida Begum was the full sister of Md. Shahid Ali and the suit property is the <em>ejmali</em> property of the co-sharers. In order to get a separate <em>saham</em> in the suit property the predecessor of the applicants, Wahida Begum filed a Partition Suit being No.192 of 2003 in the Court of learned Senior Assistant Judge, Dinajpur Sadar, which is awaiting for disposal. Furthermore, challenging the sub-kabala deed of the plaintiff from the heirs of Md. Shahid Ali, dated 14.02.1993 the predecessor of the applicant filed an Other Suit No.105 of 2008 in the 1<sup>st</sup> Court of learned Joint District Judge, Dinajpur, which is also pending for disposal and considering all these facts and circumstances the learned trial court committed no wrong in passing the impugned order dated 15.07.2018. The learned Advocate in support of his argument referred 32 DLR (AD) 170.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In order to appreciate the submission advanced from the sides of the learned counsels for the respective parties, having gone through the impugned order No.58 dated 15.07.2018 in Small Causes Case (hereinafter SCC) Suit No.01 of 2010, the application filed by the applicant-opposite parties under Order I rule 10 of the Code of Civil Procedure, the plaint of the original SCC Suit No.01 of 2010 (Annexure-A), the written statement filed by the opposite party No.1 and 2 (Annexure-B) and the additional written statement of the defendant-opposite party No.1 and 2, it transpires that the original SCC Suit No.01 of 2010 was instituted by one Anjuman Ara Begum for ejectment of tenants stating that she has purchased the suit premises from the heirs of Md. Shahid Ali , who was the owner of the suit premises by a registered sub-kabala dated 20.11.2006 at a consideration Tk.15,00,000/- (Fifteen lac). It was further contended by the plaintiff to the suit that the suit shops are very old and dilapidated, which can be broken at any time and since the defendants are defaulters in paying the rents, they are liable to be evicted from the suit premises and meanwhile the plaintiff served a notice under section 106 of the Transfer of Property Act, 1882 terminating the ‘landlord and <em>varatia’</em> relationship directing the defendant No.1 and 2 to handover the vacant possession of the suit premises. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On perusal of the written statement, which is the pleadings of the defendant No.1 and 2, I find that the defendants are the tenants under Md. Shahid Ali, the ex-landlord of the suit premises and after the death of Md. Shahid Ali his wife, sons and daughter inherited the property. The contention of the defendant No.1 and 2 as it appears from their written statement is such that the defendants are not habitual defaulter under the plaintiff and while the plaintiff denied to accept rent for the month of November and December, 2006 and January of 2007, the defendants under the ambit of Rent Control Ordinance depositing the rents regularly after filing of a Rent Control Case No.17 of 2007 and as such the defendants are not habitual defaulter and they cannot be evicted from the suit shops. It was further alleged by the contesting defendant No.1 and 2 that late Md. Shahid Ali was the owner of the suit premises and on the said premises there are some shops. On the roof of those shops after taking rent by an agreement dated 05.05.1992, the defendants have erected a Club namely Friends Club. It was further contended by the contesting defendants in their pleadings that they have paid rent at the rate of Tk.1,000/- (one thousand) per month in favour of Md. Shahid Ali according to ‘<em>varatia</em> agreement’ and after the death of Md. Shahid Ali, his successive owners also realized rent for the schedule premises at the rate of Tk.1,000/- (one thousand) per month.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the papers, facts and circumstances of the case it is noticed that the plaintiff is a subsequent purchaser from the successive landlords, who are the legal heirs of the original landlord Md. Shahid Ali and it is the case of the plaintiff that she has purchased the suit premises by a registered sub-kabala deed dated 20.11.2006. Under the ambit of Small Cause Courts Act, 1887 the landlord is empower to evict the tenant, when it is established that the tenant is a habitual defaulter in payment of rents and the landlord has basic need of the suit premises. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Consulting the case laws under reference, it is evident to note that in a suit for ejectment of tenant, as the instant case be; their lordships in the case of <em>Additional Deputy Commissioner (Revenue) and Assistant Custodian, Vested Property, Barisal –vs.- Md. Mozammel Haque and another </em>16 BLD(AD)237 have clearly held that, </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“In the application for addition of party the petitioner asserted that the property being vested property the plaintiff has no right, title and interest in the suit premises to maintain the suit for ejectment against the defendant who is a lessee from the custodian of vested property. The trial court rightly rejected the petitioner’s prayer holding, inter alia, that in a suit for an ejectment of monthly tenant the question of determination of title cannot be gone into and as such there is no necessity of the petitioner’s presence in the suit.”</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In another decision reported in 1981 BLD(AD) 128 our Apex Court held that in SCC suit, the court has no jurisdiction to go into the question of title, except incidentally, or to set aside the decree of a civil court. Besides this, this court relying upon the aforesaid decisions in the case of <em>Noor Mohammad –vs.- Md. Noor Hossain &amp; another</em> 56 DLR 53 held, in a suit for ejectment of a tenant third party, who is not claiming tenancy under the plaintiff is neither a necessary party nor a proper party.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Small Cause Courts Act (IX of 1887),</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Section 15 of the aforesaid Act, does not confer any jurisdiction to the court in a S.C.C. suit to enter into the question of title in respect of the suit premises, except incidentally or to set aside the decree passed in a civil court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the instant case, I have come across that the applicants were intended to become a party to the original SCC Suit No.01 of 2010 on the basis of co-sharership in the suit holding, and in this connection it is obvious to </span><span style="font-size: 11pt;">note that the predecessor of the applicants on the basis of her co-sharership by way of inheritance meanwhile instituted a partition suit and a separate declaratory suit challenging the sub-kabala deed of the plaintiff and both the two suits are pending for disposal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">14.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is a fact that the above mentioned suits which are pending for disposal are separate proceedings and it would be decided on merit, but in the instant suit, I find that the learned trial court failed to appraise the actual proposition of law and facts and circumstances of the case. it is to be noted here that the decisions of our Apex Court as cited in the impugned order of the learned trial court viz. 2 MLR (AD)357 is not identical with the instant case and there is apparent distinguishable facts and feature of the case on which their lordships opined that addition of co-sharers in a proceedings of SCC suit is not illegal and here in that case it is observed by their lordships that, where the co-sharers are in possession of the suit premises, their application can be entertained under the ambit of Order I rule 10 of the Code of Civil Procedure, but in the instant case it is not the case of the applicants that they are in possession of the suit premises along with the defendant No. 1 and 2.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">15.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Be that as it may, I am constrained to hold such a view that, in passing the impugned order the trial court was not justified and lawful.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">16.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the result, the Rule is made absolute without any order as to costs. The impugned order No.58 dated 15.07.2018 passed by the learned Senior Assistant Judge, Sadar, Dinajpur in SCC Suit No.01 of 2010 allowing the application for addition of party is hereby set aside.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">17.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The order of stay granted earlier by this Court at the time of issuance of the Rule stands vacated.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">18.<span style="font-variant-numeric: normal; font-variant-east-asian: normal; font-weight: normal; font-stretch: normal; font-size: 7pt; line-height: normal; font-family: 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Communicate the judgment and order at once.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-indent: .5in; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed.</span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_November_19(2)/Issue%20__November__19(2)__C.R%20_2740%20of%2018_Soumendra%20Sarker,%20J.__1.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. 2740 of 2018</span></u></em></strong></a></p></div></div></div></div>
811	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Bangladesh Maritime Carriers Ltd. Vs.  Jamuna Oil Com. Ltd and ors  </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Execution Case No. 02 of 2013  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  M. Khurshid A. Sarkar, J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Mustafizur Rahman Khan, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ   </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Bangladesh Maritime Carriers Ltd. </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Jamuna Oil Company Ltd and others  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Code of Civil Procedure </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(ADMIRALTY JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; height: 247px;" width="657"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 294.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">M. Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">06.11.2019</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 55.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_November_19(2)/Issue%20__November__19(2)__Execution%20Case%20_02%20of%2013_M.%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarker,%20J.__5.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p></td><td style="width: 263.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Bangladesh Maritime Carriers Ltd. </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Plaintiff-Judgment Debtor</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Jamuna Oil Company Ltd and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Defendant-Decree Holder</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Code of Civil Procedure (V of 1908)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Order 21</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Rules 43, 68, 69, 77, 78 and 79</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Whether the executing Court is competent to cancel the auction after confirming the auction-sale:<u></u></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.2pt;">Once the auction-sale is confirmed by the executing Court upon being satisfied that the auction-purchaser has complied with the Directions and Orders issued/passed by the executing Court from time to time, including the payment of the consideration money within the stipulated time, then there is no scope for the executing Court to show any sympathy to the Judgment-Debtor even if the Judgment-Debtor pays full decreetal amount together with a further amount of solatium after confirmation of auction-sale.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> .....(12)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Mr. Mustafizur Rahman Khan, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the Plaintiff-Applicant</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Mr. Kamal Ul Alam, Senior Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the Respondant No. 1</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Mr. Anik R. Haque</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the Auction-Purchaser</span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">M. Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">By filing this application, the plaintiff (Judgment-Debtor) is praying for recalling the Order dated 13.08.2018 passed by this Court confirming auction-sale of the coastal tanker M.T. ASHA held on 20.03.2018 and for accepting an amount of Tk. 39,38,372/- under Payment Order No. 0946692/215 dated 22.09.2018 in satisfaction of the decreetal amount in Admiralty Suit No. 05 of 2002 with a further amount of Tk. 4,59,500/- as solatium vide Pay Order No. 1002200/215 dated 03.02.2019 made out in the name of the auction-purchaser. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Succinctly, the background facts of filing the instant application is that the Plaintiff-Judgment Debtor (hereinafter, “the plaintiff”) filed Admiralty Suit No. 05 of 2002 for realization of Tk. 31,81,709.80 along with interest @ 18% as freight bills against the principal defendants of the suit. The defendant No. 1 (Jamuna Oil Company Ltd) contested the suit by filing written statement on 07.08.2002, denying the material allegations of the plaint, and making a counter-claim of Tk. 39,38,371.47 alleging short landing of its cargo by the plaintiff. The said Admiralty Suit No. 5 of 2002 was dismissed for default on 18.03.2010. By the Judgment and Order dated 10.03.2011, the counter-claim of the defendant No. 1 was decreed in favour of the defendant No. 1 and against the plaintiff for an amount of Tk. 39,38,371.47 and, against the said Judgment and Order, the plaintiff filed Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 1819 of 2011, which was dismissed by the Hon’ble Appellate Division by its Judgment and Order dated 15.11.2015. Against the aforesaid Judgment dated 15.11.2015, the plaintiff filed Civil Review Petition No. 173 of 2016, which was pending before the Hon’ble Appellate Division at the time of filing the instant application and, subsequently, it has been dismissed for default (non-appearance) on 15.11.2018. Meanwhile, the defendant No. 1 as decree-holder filed the instant Execution Case No. 02 of 2013, and had the coastal tanker M.T. ASHA attached for sale through auction. The plaintiff filed an application on 23.10.2017 praying for stay of the auction-sale along with an account-payee cheque for an amount of Tk. 39,38,372/- equivalent to the decreetal amount. Upon hearing the application, this Court passed an Order dated 23.10.2017 staying the auction proceedings and, upon considering the ill health of the Managing Director of the plaintiff-company, allowed until 23.02.2018 for encashment of the said cheque, ordering that otherwise a proceeding shall be caused under Section 138 of the Negotiable Instruments Act, 1881(shortly, NI Act). As the plaintiff was unable to arrange for encashment of the cheque, this Court by Order dated 27.02.2018 asked the plaintiff to show cause as to why a proceeding under the NI Act shall not be initiated against it, and further vacated the Order of stay on auction proceedings and directed the Marshall to take steps for auction-sale of the vessel. The auction notice was published on 10.03.2018, and the auction was held on 20.03.2018. On the day of the auction i.e. 20.03.2018, the auction-purchaser, Al-Haj Abul Kalam Azad (Babul), Proprietor M/s Padma Ship Recycling Industries, bid an amount of Tk. 1,05,70,700/-, which was the highest bid for the vessel, submitting a Pay Order of 10% of the bid-money as earnest money. Against the Order dated 20.03.2018 holding the auction, the plaintiff filed CMP No. 361 of 2018, along with a Bank Guarantee for the decreetal amount, and the Hon’ble Judge-in-Chambers was pleased to pass an Order dated 27.03.2018 staying the auction and directed for the Bank Guarantee to be kept with the Registrar General of the Supreme Court, where it remains till date unencashed. The ensuing Civil Petition for Leave to Appeal No. 2573 of 2018, however, was dismissed by Order dated 07.08.2018. Thereafter, the auction-sale was confirmed by this Court’s Order dated 13.08.2018. Now, when an application by the auction-purchaser for a direction to deliver the vessel is pending before this Court, the plaintiff has come up with this application praying for recalling this Court’s above-mentioned Order dated 13.08.2018, upon depositing two separate Pay Orders, one for satisfaction of the decreetal amount and another in the name of the auction-purchaser as solatium.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The auction-purchaser is contesting this application by filing written objection contending, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter-alia</em>, that the Judgment-Debtor (plaintiff) having exhausted all the stages in the suit and, thereafter, again all the stages in the execution case, now has come up with this device with a malafide intention to abuse the process of this Court and simply attempting to harass this bonafide auction-purchaser. The auction held on 20.03.2018 was a continuation of the auction process that was initiated by publication of auction notices 1st time on 17.10.2017. The Judgment-Debtor, including his counsel in person, has made several representations or promises to this Court for paying off the decreetal amount, but ultimately it proved that the Judgment-Debtor persistently flouted with the Court proceedings and obtained unfair advantage to delay the process of execution. It is stated that the Judgment-Debtor obtained stay of the auction 1<sup>st</sup> time on 23.10.2017 by misleading this Court with a cheque for paying the decreetal amount, but the cheque was dishonored. The Judgment-Debtor also misled the Hon'ble Appellate Division by presenting a Bank Guarantee which was encashable after 6 (six) months and also presenting blank cheque instead of Pay Order as per the direction of the Court, which the Appellate Division refused to accept.  </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Mustafizur Rahman Khan, the learned Advocate appearing for the Judgment-Debtor contends that there has been serious illegalities in calling and holding the auction for selling the vessel inasmuch as the auction-sale was held on 20.03.2018, while the notice for such auction-sale was given only on 10.03.2018; that is to say, there was only 10 (ten) days between the notice and the auction. By taking me through Order 21 Rule 68 of the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908 (CPC), he submits that in the case of property of the kind described in the Proviso to Order 21 Rule 43 of the CPC, no sale in execution shall, without the consent in writing of the Judgment-Debtor, take place until after the expiration of at least 30 (thirty) days in the case of immovable property, and of at least 15 (fifteen) days in the case of movable property, calculated from the date on which the copy of the proclamation has been affixed on the Court-house of the Judge ordering the sale and the proclamation has to be in the form prescribed under Order 21 Rule 66 of the CPC. He submits that the Proviso of Order 21 Rule 43 of the CPC is inapplicable in the instant case in that the said provision concerns goods which are subject to speedy and natural decay or when the expense of keeping it in custody is likely to exceed its value. In an effort to elaborate his above submissions, he contends that in the instant case, the first proclamation that approximates the requirement of Order 21 Rule 66 of the CPC was not published until 10.03.2018 and, hence, the property intended to be sold being a movable property, the auction-sale ought not to have occurred until 25.03.2018. He submits that the requirement under Order 21 Rule 68 of the CPC is a substantive requirement of law, as opposed to a procedural one, in view of the provision of Order 21 Rule 69(3) of the CPC, which provides that every sale shall be stopped if, before the lot is knocked down, the debt and costs including the costs of the sale, are tendered to the officer conducting sale, or proof is given to his satisfaction that the amount of such debt and costs have been paid into Court which ordered the sale. According to Mr. Khan, Order 21 Rule 69(3) of the CPC gives an opportunity to the Judgment-Debtor to pay off the decreetal amount along with costs, even after the proclamation of sale of 15 (fifteen) days in case of a movable property, before any auction takes place, unless the Judgment-Debtor has consented to a shorter period under Order 21 Rule 68 of the CPC. He argues that since in the instant case, the plaintiff had never consented to a shorter period under Order 21 Rule 68 of the CPC, the auction suffers from an illegality for violating the said provisions of Order 21 Rule 68 of the CPC, which is to the prejudice of the rights to property of the plaintiff. Mr. Khan forcefully submits that this is a serious illegality, which cannot be regarded as a procedural irregularity within the terms of Order 21 Rule 78 of the CPC not vitiating the sale. In an effort to buttress up his argument on this issue, he refers to the case of Narayan Chandra Vs Manhar Mandal 43 DLR(AD) 152 and submits that on the ground of non-compliance of these provisions the Appellate Division set aside the auction-sale held in the afore-cited case. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He, then, alleges that as per the plaintiff’s claim, the market value of the vessel is about 20 (twenty) crore, but the vessel has been sold in auction only at 1 (one) crore and odds. He contends that it was the duty of the concerned officials of the Admiralty Section of this Court to either appoint a valuer for assessment of the value of the vessel or to take information from the market by appointing a surveyor regarding the price and, then, place the same to the Hon’ble Presiding Judge of the Admiralty Court, and had the value of the vessel been assessed before inviting the auction, the Hon’ble Presiding Judge would not have agreed to accept the bid at such a low price. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Khan next alleges that the plaintiff has deposited a Bank Guarantee of the decreetal amount before the Hon’ble Appellate Division on 27.03.2018 which is kept under the safe custody of the Registrar General, who is the Marshall of this Court, and till date it remains uncashed. But this information was not disclosed to the Hon’ble Presiding Judge of the Admiralty Court at the time of filing the application for confirmation of auction-sale on 13.08.2018. He contends that had this information been placed before the Hon’ble Presiding Judge on 13.08.2018, the auction-sale would not have been confirmed by the Hon’ble Presiding Judge. He argues that because of obtaining this confirmation Order, the auction-purchaser is now taking recourse to the relevant provisions of the CPC to defeat the plaintiff’s right.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He makes a humble prayer before this Court to apply the principles of equity in this case, pointing out to a number incidents took place in this suit; such as (i) the plaintiff’s suit was not professionally conducted by the filing lawyer, for, the suit was, at first, dismissed for default and, thereafter, it was not restored, (ii)<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the defendant’s counter-claim was decreed <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">exparte</em> simply on the findings that there was a short delivery of only 1,49,746 liters of diesel out of 1866.56 Metric Tons and (iii) the auction was held without obtaining any valuation of the vessel. He argues that had the plaintiff been able to produce his witnesses (PWs), there was a fair chance to establish his case that it was the concerned staffs of the defendant No. 1 who were liable for the short delivery. By referring to the case of Denim Attires Ltd Vs Iffat Obaid and others reported in 2019 ALR(AD) Online 107<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>(CP No. 2592 of 2017, Judgment delivered on 11.03.2018), he submits that the Hon’ble Appellate Division granted equitable relief in the cited case, even after the property was delivered to the auction-purchaser by executing the registered deed of sale following<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the auction-sale. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Per contra, Mr. Anik R. Haque, the learned Advocate appearing for the auction-purchaser submits that the Hon’ble Appellate Division has affirmed both the original Judgments and Decree and the auction-sale in the execution case, and the Appellate Division having not found any legal infirmity in the Orders passed by the High Court Division upheld the auction-sale on both the occasions. By placing the provisions of Order 21 Rule 77(2) of the CPC, Mr. Haque submits that upon payment of the purchase-money, the auction-sale has been finalized and the sale has become absolute and the auction-purchaser has acquired the legal title in the property which cannot be taken away or circumvented. He submits that it is now an obligation for the executing Court to deliver the moveable property to the auction-purchaser under Order 21 Rule 79 of the CPC. By referring to the case of Fariduddin Chowdhury Vs. Sylhet Gas Works Ltd 1995 BLT (AD) 168 and the case of Sonali Bank Vs. Artharin Adalat 15 MLR (AD) 20, Mr. Haque submits that once the auction is completed, no relief is available against such auction-sale, as there is no provision in any law or in Order 21 of the CPC to set aside a confirmation of sale in case of moveable property. He submits that once the sale is confirmed and made absolute, the Judgment-Debtor losses his right to receive back the property in question even on satisfying the decreetal amount. He argues that if the confirmation of sale is set aside in the present case, it will tantamount to declaring the title of the auction-purchaser nugatory, thereby, extending and giving an unwarranted benevolence to the Judgment-Debtor. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He submits that the auction-sale was conducted as per the law in compliance with Order 21 Rule 68 of the CPC. He further submits that the specification of time in Order 21 Rule 68 of the CPC is merely a procedural law, which is confirmed by Order 21 Rule 78 of the CPC which provides that an auction-sale concerning a moveable property will not be vitiated due to an irregularity and, thus, it is open to the Judgment-Debtor to institute suit against the person responsible for the irregularity, if any, in conducting the auction-sale provided the Judgment-Debtor has sustained an injury. He contends that, in this case, the Judgment-Debtor will not be able to show that it has sustained an injury owing to such irregularity, because the Judgment-Debtor has been avoiding to pay the decreetal amount in the last 6 (six) years by abusing the process of the Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Haque lastly submits that in view of the dubious conduct of the Judgment-Debtor in an effort to frustrate the execution of the decree, it is clear that he has not come in clean hands before this Court and, as such, he is not entitled to plea for equitable relief. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">One day the plaintiff (Judgment-Debtor) having appeared in person in the Court-room was telling so many stories by wailing and lamentation regarding this suit and prayed for not to dispose of the application summarily. Pursuant thereto, this Court assured him that the Court would take his statements into consideration by examining all the relevant papers, Order-sheets and the applicable laws. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Upon hearing the learned Advocate for the auction-purchaser and the learned Advocate for the Judgment-Debtor (plaintiff), perusing the Judgment and Decree (<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">exparte</em>) dated 10.03.2011 passed by the Admiralty Court in the Admiralty Suit No. 05 of 2002, the Judgment and Order dated 15.11.2015 passed by the Appellate Division in the CP No. 1819 of 2011, which was preferred against the aforesaid Judgment and Decree dated 10.03.2011, the entire Order-sheets of the suit as well as the execution case and examining the all the provisions of Order 21 of the CPC together with relevant case-laws, it appears to this Court that there is hardly any scope for this Court to recall the Order dated 13.08.2018 by which the auction was confirmed inasmuch as this Court, upon exhausting all the formalities for execution of the decree, has eventually confirmed the auction-sale of the coastal tanker MT ASHA held on 20.03.2018. It is the settled law of this jurisdiction that once the auction-sale is confirmed by the executing Court upon being satisfied that the auction-purchaser has complied with the Directions and Orders issued/passed by the executing Court from time to time, including the payment of the consideration money within the stipulated time, then there is no scope for the executing Court to show any sympathy to the Judgment-Debtor even if the Judgment-Debtor pays full decreetal amount together with a further amount of solatium after confirmation of auction-sale. In this case, it is apparent that after confirmation of auction-sale the Judgment-Debtor (plaintiff), having managed the funds, has deposited a Pay Order of the decreetal amount together with a Pay Order for an amount of Tk. 4,59,500/- as solatium vide Pay Order No. 1002200/215 dated 03.02.2019, however, this Court is unable to exercise its discretion at this stage. While it is evident from the record that this suit was dealt with by his previous engaged lawyer in a very cavalier fashion, there is no provision in the law to help the plaintiff at the fag end of the execution of a lawful decree. This Court has taken note of the facts that (i) the original suit was dismissed for default, but the engaged lawyer of that time did not restore the suit within the prescribed time and consequently this plaintiff missed the chance to prove his case by adducing relevant witnesses before the trial Court<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>as to whether the Judgment-Debtor (plaintiff) was<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>responsible for the shortage of delivery or the Jamuna Oil Company (defendant) was liable for the said shortage and (ii) after the suit was dismissed for default, the plaintiff’s engaged lawyer again missed the chance to contest the counter-claim and eventually the original suit was decreed <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">exparte</em>. It is worthwhile to note here that the basis of <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">exparte</em> decree is allegation against the plaintiff that he has misappropriated the diesel, but the Hon’ble Appellate Division has not agreed with the said findings, albeit the plaintiff’s appeal was dismissed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: .1pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Be that as it may, from a minute perusal of the Order sheets, it transpires that when the execution case was kicked off, the Judgment-Debtor (plaintiff) was struggling to manage <span style="letter-spacing: .1pt;">required funds for depositing before the executing Court to meet up the decreetal amount, and for this purpose he was taking time form this Court again and again but ultimately he failed hopelessly. And, eventually, this Court did not have any option other than to confirm the auction-sale. At a belated stage, when the Judgment-Debtor (plaintiff) managed the funds to deposit before this Court against the decreetal amount and also for an amount of solatium, by now, this Court has become powerless to do anything for this Judgment-Debtor (plaintiff).</span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: .1pt;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: .1pt;">This Court rejects the plaintiff’s allegation that the vessel has been sold in auction at a shockingly low price, for, the auction was invited twice through publishing advertisements in the daily newspapers. Although it was incumbent upon the concerned officials of the administrative wing of the Admiralty Court to obtain a valuation report through a surveyor or through the concerned business forum, however, because of not placing the valuation report before the Hon’ble Presiding Judge of the Admiralty Court, it cannot now be hold that the auction-sale has been illegal. But I would record here that it would have been a fairer practice on part of Advocate M. Golam Arshed, who had filed the application for confirmation of auction-sale, had he disclosed the facts of depositing the Bank Guarantee of decreetal amount by the plaintiff before the Hon’ble Appellate Division, which still remains uncashed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 112%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 112%; letter-spacing: .1pt;">The learned Advocate for the Judgment-Debtor (plaintiff) has tried his best to make out a case by referring to the case of Denim Attires Ltd Vs Iffat Obaid and others reported in 2019 ALR (AD) Online 107 (CP No. 2592</span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> conduct of proceedings in an Artha Rin Adalat. In the case of M/S. Antibiotic Stores and others Vs. Subordinate Judge and Artha Rin Adalat reported in 8 MLR(AD) page 4 this Division again observed that under Section 5(4) of the Artha Rin Adalat Ain, 1990, the Artha Rin Adalat is a Civil Court and subject to the provisions of the Ain, the Artha Rin Adalat have all the powers and jurisdictions under the Code of Civil Procedure, 1908.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Since the instant auction was held under Artha Rin Adalat Ain, 1990 which did not provide specific procedure to be followed for holding auction and as to time limit for payment of auction money, the Adalat followed the provision of the Code of Civil Procedure rightly. Consequently, we do not find any force in the submissions of Mr. Golam Arshed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Accordingly, we find substance in the appeal.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 112%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo2; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 112%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Thus, the appeal is allowed. Judgment and order of the High Court Division is set aside. The impugned orders of the Adalat are hereby declared to have been passed without lawful authority and are of no legal effect. The Adalat shall proceed with the Execution Case in accordance with law.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-indent: .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Ed.</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; letter-spacing: .1pt;"> </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_November_19(2)/Issue%20__November__19(2)__Execution%20Case%20_02%20of%2013_M.%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarker,%20J.__5.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;">Execution Case No. 02 of 2013</span></u></strong></a></p></div></div></div></div>
812	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Cathay Pacific Airways Ltd. Vs.  Vantage International Limited.  </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Company Matter No. 43 of 2007  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  M. Khurshid A. Sarker, J </p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Dr. Sharif Bhuiyan with  Mr. Tanim Hussain Shawon, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(2) LNJ   </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Cathay Pacific Airways Limited </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Vantage International Limited  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Company Act </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%; letter-spacing: -.3pt;">(STATUTORY ORIGINAL JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; height: 332px;" width="642"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 287.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="line-height: 110%; margin: 0in -1.4pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; letter-spacing: -.3pt; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">M. Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-right: -1.45pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Judgment on</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">23.05.2019</span></strong></p></td><td style="width: 53.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_November_19(2)/Issue%20__November__19(2)__Com.%20Mat.%20_43%20of%2007_M.%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarker,%20J.__4.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol;
