line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">}</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_November_19(2)/Issue%20__November__19(2)__Com.%20Mat.%20_295_151%20of%2018_M.%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarker,%20J.__2.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;">}</span></span></span></a></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; line-height: 200%; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p><p align="center" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="text-align: center; margin: 0in -1.1pt 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> </span></p></td><td style="width: 266.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;"><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">A.K.M. Lutful Kabir and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Petitioners</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Md. Shahjahan and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Respondents</span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">(in Company Matter No.295 of 2018)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"> </span></p><p class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Neeshorgo Hotel &amp; Resort Limitd and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">. . .</span></strong> <strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Respondents</span></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoBodyTextIndent" style="margin: 0in; margin-bottom: .0001pt; text-align: right;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-ansi-language: EN; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p><strong style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 233 (3)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; letter-spacing: -.2pt;"><br/>The Legislature intended to<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>resolve all types of disputes or grievances arising out of the Companies Act expeditiously through a higher rank of Court i. e. either the District Court or the High Court Division, in a summary manner so as to help smoothly flourish the business and commerce without experiencing protracted, time-consuming and complex procedures which are required to be followed/observed/applied by the Civil Courts and, therefore, most of the Company Matters relating to/arising out of/in connection with the grievance of any members of the company or debenture holder of the company are tried/adjudicated upon without taking any oral evidence. However, it does not necessarily mean that the Company Court is not competent to dispose of a company case by taking oral evidance, because there is no provision within the four corners of the Companies Act prohibiting the Company Court to take oral evidence. Rather, the expressions employed in Section 233(3) of the Companies Act, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“If after hearing the parties present on the date……”,</em> implies that there may be petitioner witness/es (PW/s) or respondent witness/es (RW/s) or the Court witnesses/es (CW/s) if the facts and circumstances so warrant, inasmuch as this Court requires to form an opinion <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“If the Court is of the opinion”, </em>(the wordings of Section 233 (3) of the Companies Act) for passing necessary Order and/or Direction.</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                             </span>...(32)<u></u></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Companies Act (XVIII of 1994)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Sections 90 to 100</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">A Director is a person who is elected by the majority members entrusting upon him/her day-to-day business activities and finances and, also, to ensure that all statutory filing obligations are met. Thus, the Directors of the company in true sense are the ‘trustees’ of the company. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">       </span>...(37)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Companies Act (XVIII of 1994)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 233</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">When the Court is of the opinion that the interest of the petitioner of a Section-233 application is being prejudicially affected, it may pass any Order it deems fit, as mandated by the Legislature in Section 233(3) of the Companies Act. Accordingly, in exercising the power vested in this Court under Section 233(3) of the Companies Act, this Court is well empowered to pass an Order decreeing that a Director is hereby declared to be ‘disqualified’ or the offices of a Director is hereby declared to have been ‘vacated’. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">          </span>...(40)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Companies Act (XVIII of 1994)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 233 and 233(3)<u></u></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The powers invested in the Court under Section 233(3) of the Companies Act is wider and superior than the power given to the Court by any other provisions of the Companies Act. By virtue of the power under Section 233(3) of the Companies Act, the Court is competent to order the company to conduct its audit, to appoint an Independent Auditor and to fix the remuneration of the Auditor, to direct the company for calling and holding any meeting (which may be Board meeting, EGM or AGM) and to make any necessary Order/Directions <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">‘to regulate the conduct of the company’s affairs’</em> (the expression engraved in Section 233(3)(b) of the Companies Act). However, since the power invested in this Court under Section 233(3) of the Companies Act is discretionary in nature, it should be exercised by this Court judiciously in the rarest of rare cases only upon carrying out meticulous examination of the facts and circumstance of an application under Section 233 of the Companies Act. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>...(41)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Companies Act (XVIII of 1994)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Section 94(1) and 108(2)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">An incorporated company is competent to insert in its Articles of Association any provisions of disqualification in the matter of becoming a Director by virtue of the company’s power given in Section 94(2) of the Companies Act, in addition to the provisions relating to disqualifications for the Directors set out in Section 94(1) of the Companies Act. Also, under Section 108(2) of the Companies Act, a company is empowered to incorporate other provisions as the grounds for vacating the office of the Directors provided in Section 108(1) of the Companies Act. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">          </span>...(44)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Companies Act (XVIII of 1994)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">Sections 85(3), 94(1) and 108(2)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; tab-stops: right 210.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">The Company Court acts as the ‘Ombudsman’ of the companies; meaning that normally the Company Court will not interfere with the internal affairs of the company, but if the situation demands, then the Court shall do the needful. While only in a few circumstances, this Court is competent to <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suo motu</em> interfere with the management of the company, however, in most of the events, this Court is allowed to look into the affairs of the company upon receiving an application. This is the scheme of enactment of Company Laws in most of the countries around the world. Any action taken or omissions occured either by the member/s of the Board (such as, Director, Managing Director and Chairman) or by the agent/s of the company (such as, Company Secretary, General Manager, Accounts Officer and other Officers) in running/managing the affairs of the company, may be examined by this Court either <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suo motu</em> or on receiving application. For example, the Legislature has vested the power in this Court to <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suo motu</em> direct the company to call, hold and conduct any meeting (Board Meeting, Extraordinary General Meeting, Annual General Meeting) when the situation described in Section 85(3) so warrants and, in dealing with the above situation, the Company Court is also empowered to pass any ancilliary, consequential and supplementary Order and Directions, including passing Order for appointment of auditor, fixing its remuneration, etc. <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                                      </span>...(48)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">A.K.M. Lutful Kabir and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the Petitioners</span></u></em></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(in Company Matter No.151 of 2018)</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Md. Shahjahan and others</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"> For the P</span></u></em></strong><strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">etitioners</span></u></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(in Company Matter No.295 of 2018)</span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: 1.0in; text-align: justify; text-indent: .5in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. S.M. Atikur Rahman, Advocate</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 5.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the Petitioners</span></u></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Mustafizur Rahman Khan with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; text-align: justify; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the respondent nos. 2-5,7-8,11-15</span></u></em></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: right; line-height: 110%;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Asif Bin Anwar, Advocates</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 4.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></em></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . . <u>For the Petitioners</u></span></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; line-height: 150%;"><span style="font-size: 5.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr. A M Aminuddin, Senior Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr. Sakib Rejwan Kabir, Advocates</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 5.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></em></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the Respondents Nos.2-6</span></u></em></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in; line-height: 150%;"><span style="font-size: 4.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 150%; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr. A M Aminuddin, Senior Advocate with</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-left: .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-weight: bold; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Mr. Md. Minhaduzzaman, Advocates</span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 5.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;"> </span></em></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">. . .</span></em></strong> <strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">For the Respondents Nos.</span></u></em></strong><u> </u><strong><em><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">11-48</span></u></em></strong></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">(In Company Matter No. 295 of 2018) </span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 7.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="text-decoration: none;"> </span></span></u></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">M. Khurshid Alam Sarkar, J. </span></u></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Since, in both the Company Matters, common questions of law and facts are involved and the parties of these two matters are the same set of persons and, more so, the <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">lis</em> is centring around the common property, they are taken up together and disposed of by a single Judgment. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Company Matter No. 151 of 2018</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In Company Matter No. 151 of 2018, the petitioners (who are the respondent nos. 8 &amp; 9 of the Company Matter No. 295 of 2018) challenges the resolution dated 20.04.2018 taken by the respondent nos. 2 to 15 in the Extraordinary General Meeting (EGM) of Neeshorgo Hotel &amp; Resort Limited (hereinafter referred to either as the respondent no. 1 or as the company) and, also, the conduct/activities of the respondents in running the affairs of the company in a manner prejudicial to the interests of the company. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The facts of the Company Matter No. 151 of 2018, briefly, are that the petitioners are the shareholder-Directors of the company which was incorporated as a private company limited by shares on 27.01.2016 under the Companies Act, 1994 (hereinafter referred to as the Companies Act). The company is engaged in running the business of hotel and resort, currently at only one spot, at Plot 492, Kolatoli, Marine Drive Road, Cox's Bazar, where a multistoried building had already been constructed with more than 100 (one hundred) studio apartments with facilities of a hotel and resort by Khettra Architects Limited, a Developer-company, in which the petitioner nos. 1 and 2 are the Managing Director and the Chairman respectively. The name of this iconic building was given ‘Neeshorgo’. While the landowner was owning 60% of the spaces/flats of the said iconic building and the Developer-company was owning 40% of its spaces/flats, they sold the bulk of their respective proportions to the present flat owners, and till now the landowner and the Developer-company own a considerable part of the ‘Neeshorgo’. The flat owners, which include the Managing Director and the Chairman of the Developer-company, of ‘Neeshorgo’ and members of their families purchased the shares of the company and as such all the shareholders of the company are either flat owners of the ‘Neeshorgo’ or their family-members. The company was incorporated with an authorized share capital of Taka 10,0000000/- (ten crore) divided into 1,000000/- (one crore) ordinary shares of Taka 10/- (ten) each and<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>27 shareholders were issued 30,00,000 (thirty lacs) shares of Taka 10 (ten) each and, out of the above shares, in the name of petitioner nos. 1 &amp; 2, 4,00,000/- (four lacs) shares of Taka 10 (ten) each were issued. As per Article 21 of the Articles of Association (AoA) of the company, the company has 21 Directors. The petitioner no. 1 was nominated as the first Chairman and the petitioner no. 2 was appointed as the first Managing Director of the company for a period of 5 years and the respondent nos. 2 to 15 were nominated shareholder-Directors of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is stated that the company could not hold its first Annual General Meeting (AGM) since its incorporation due to not being able to complete its financial accounts properly, for which the company formed a committee which gave its report on 04.07.2017. The Bank accounts of the company were being operated under the joint signatures of the petitioner nos. 1 and 2 along with another Director Mr. Mijanur Rahman. But due to the temporary absence of the said Mijanur Rahman, the cheques of the company were being signed by the petitioners and when objection was raised regarding withdrawal of money without the signature of Mr. Mijanur Rahman, in the 10<sup>th</sup> Board Meeting of the company held on 29.09.2017, it was unanimously decided that another Director, Dr. Md. Tajul Islam, should also be included as a co-signatory, whose signature shall be mandatory. Thereafter, the respondent nos. 2 to 15 served a Legal Notice dated 26.11.2017 upon the petitioners seeking explanations on certain matters and, eventually, also issued a requisition notice dated 31.01.2018 upon the Board of Directors of the company to hold an EGM of the company with the agenda of appointment of a new Managing Director and Chairman of the company and the matters relating to the present state of affairs and management of the company. Thereafter, the respondent nos. 2 to 15 held an EGM of the company on 20.04.2018 wherein resolutions were taken to remove the petitioners from the position of the Chairman and the Managing Director, and the respondent nos. 12 and 8 were appointed as the new Chairman and the Managing Director of the company. Hence, this petition.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The respondent nos. 2-5, 7-8 &amp; 11-15 (who are the petitioners of the Company Matter No. 295 of 2018) contest the case by filing an affidavit-in-opposition contending, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">inter alia</em>, that the petitioner nos. 1 and 2 as the Chairman and the Managing Director of the company were managing the day-to-day affairs of the company from the very beginning in the most illegitimate, illegal and prejudicial manner in connivance with M Ershad Hossain, Md. Jashim Uddin Bhuiyan, Mohammad Jalaluddin, Md. Fazle Rabbi Khan and Supti Chowdhury (respondent nos. 2-6 of the Company Matter No. 295 of 2018), who are also the shareholders and Directors of the company. The petitioner nos. 1 and 2 submitted a letter dated 06.03.2016 to the Social Islami Bank Limited (the Bank), in which the company maintains a Bank account, requesting to change the operating instructions of the Bank account so that cheques are honoured with the signatures of the petitioner nos. 1 and 2 only, altering the instruction pursuant to the 1st Board resolution dated 05.0<span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">2.2</span>016, which required another Director’s (Mr. ATM Mijanur Rahman's) signature mandatorily for signing of the cheques with signature of either the petitioner no. 1 or 2. In the said letter, the petitioner nos. 1 and 2 mentioned that a Board meeting was held on 05.03<em>.</em>2016 and included an extract of the minutes of the said Board meeting quoting that it was resolved in the said Board meeting that a decision of agenda no. 7 of the meeting held on 05.02.2016 has been reviewed and discussed elaborately and for smooth functioning of the company, it has been decided that the account will henceforth be operated by any two of the three Directors namely, petitioner nos. 1 and 2 and ATM Mijanur Rahman. It is alleged that no such Board meeting was ever held and as such the contents of the letter dated 06.03.2016 are utterly false and the extracts of the Board meeting incorporated are wholly fictitious. The petitioner nos. 1 and 2 admitted the aforesaid allegation in the 10<sup>th</sup> Board meeting and also in the reply to the Legal Notice dated 05.12.2017. Since, as the Managing Director and the Chairman of the company, the petitioner nos. 1 and 2 have committed the above illegalities, since they have failed to conduct the 1<sup>st</sup> AGM so far in violation of Article 19 of the AoA and Section 81 of the Companies Act, since they have indefinitely postponed the date of AGM fixed by the Board upon cancelling the appointment of an audit firm by the petitioner no. 2 vide letter dated 23.01.2019, and since they are diverting the income of the company by collecting the rent payable by guests through the Credit Card Machine of Marine Drive Restaurant which belongs to M Ershad Hossain (the respondent no. 2 in the Company Matter No. 295 2018), the respondents having been aggrieved by the conduct of the petitioner nos. 1 and 2 called an EGM on 20.04.2018 and, vide an extraordinary resolution passed in the EGM, removed the petitioner nos. 1 and 2 from their positions of the Chairman and the Managing Director of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. SM Atiqur Rahman, the learned Advocate appearing for the petitioners, took me through the averments made in the petition and, side by side, the Memorandum of Association (MoA) and AoA of the company, and contends that the company is the brainchild of these two petitioners and, accordingly, they were appointed the Chairman and the Managing Director of the company. He contends that in the course of running the company, when the Chairman and the Managing Director were experiencing difficulties to deal with the day-to-day expenses for not getting the mandatory signature from Mr. Mijanur Rahman, they sent a letter to the Bank in good faith for relaxing the condition for encashing the cheques. By admitting the respondents’ allegations, he contends that the same may, at best, be termed as an irregularity, but not as an illegality of any sort. Mr. S.M. Atiqur Rahman, then, took me through Articles 27 and 29 of the AoA of the company and submits that before expiry of the petitioners’ tenure of 5 (five) years, removal of the petitioners from the posts of the Chairman and the Managing Director was not a fair decision by the respondents for a mere irregularity.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Per contra, Mr. Asif Bin Anwar, the learned Advocate for the respondents, takes me through the requisition notice of the EGM, enquiry notice, notice of the EGM and the resolution of the EGM, and submits that they have conducted the Extraordinary General Meeting in strict compliance with the provisions of the Companies Act and particularly in compliance with the provisions of Sections 84 and 87 of the Companies Act in that the requisition notice of the EGM was sent on 31.01.2018, thereafter, having no response, an enquiry notice was sent on 11.03<em>.</em>2018, soon after which the notice of the EGM was sent on 27.03.2018 and all of the members who attended the EGM voted in favour of the resolution passed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the respondents alleges that after knowing about the resolution impugned herein this case, the petitioner nos. 1 and 2 prompted M Ershad Hossain, Md. Jashim Uddin Bhuiyan, Mohammad Jalaluddin, Md. Fazle Rabbi Khan and Supti Chowdhury, respondent nos. 2-6 of the Company Matter No. 295 of 2018, to form a Partnership Firm imitating the company’s name, under the signboard of Neeshorgo Management Enterprise (hereinafter referred to either as ‘the Enterprise’ or as ‘the respondent no. 7’ of the Company Matter No. 295 of 2018). He further alleges that, thereafter, they, upon forming the aforesaid Enterprise, started to divert the business of the company to the said Enterprise by prejudicing the interest of the company and its shareholders. He submits that since the petitioners committed gross misconduct and acted against the interest of the company, as such all of them are liable to be disqualified from the position of the Directors of the company. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">             </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In this Company Matter No. 151 of 2018, the learned Advocate for the petitioners and the learned Advocate for the respondents were making their respective contentions and counter contentions for days together, towards receving a full-fledged Judgment and, eventually, before the date of pronouncement of this Judgment, the learned Advocate for the petitioners, Mr. SM Atikur Rahman, made a humble prayer before this Court that the petitioners shall not proceed with this matter further and will not challenge the legality and propriety of the extraordinary resolution dated 20.04.2018, if the contesting respondents, namely, respondent nos. 7-8 &amp; 11-15 do not raise any objection to keep these petitioners in the Board of the company as mere Directors of the company, for, the petitioners as the founding Chairman and the founding Managing Director of the company wish to see that the company is progressing at a gallop by overcoming all the hurdles. He contends that they shall cooperate with the respondents to remove any mismanagement in the company and misunderstanding among the shareholders of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">10.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">At this juncture, this Court asked the learned Advocate for the above-mentioned respondents as to whether the respondents would agree to keep the petitioners as the Directors of the company and, in reply thereto, the learned Advocate contended that, in fact, these respondents want to run the company not only with the cooperation of these 2 (two) petitioners, but also with six other Directors who have set up a separate business, as a Partnership Firm, under the name and style of ‘Neeshorgo Management Enterprise’ in the same plaza. He contends that in the said EGM dated 20.04.2018, no decision has been taken to remove these two petitioners as the Directors of the company. He contends that the decision in the said EGM was taken to remove them only from the posts of the Managing Director and the Chairman.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">11.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the above agreement among the parties of this matter, that the decision taken in the EGM dated 20.04.2018 would remain valid and these two petitioners shall serve as the Directors of the company, the Company Matter No. 151 of 2018 does not require framing of any issue for adjudication, rather the same deserves to be ordered by this Court to have been disposed of on compromise. Accordingly, appropriate Orders will be passed for the Company Matter No. 151 of 2018 in the operative part of this Judgment, after dealing with the factual and legal issues of the Company Matter No. 295 of 2018. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Company Matter No. 295 of 2018:</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>The background against which the Company Matter No. 295 of 2018 has been filed by the majority respondents of the Company Matter No. 151 of 2018, succinctly, is that the petitioners are the Directors of the company and collectively own 9,00,000 (nine lacs) shares out of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>30,00,000 (thirty lacs) issued shares of the company, and they have filed this petition invoking Section 233 of the Companies Act seeking the following remedies; (a) removing the respondent nos. 8 and 9 (who are the petitioners of Company Matter No. 151 of 2018) from their positions of the Managing Director and the Chairman of the company respectively, (b) removing the respondent nos. 8 and 9 from their positions as the Directors of the company and (c) removing the respondent nos. 2-6 from their positions as the Directors of the company on the ground that the respondent nos. 8 and 9 in connivance with the respondent nos. 2-6, have formed a partnership business with almost a similar name “Neeshorgo Management Enterprise”, establishing completely a parallel business of the company with a motive to exterminate the company by runing the same business at the same spot upon diverting the business of the company to the said partnership business out of greed to earn more benefit, by prejudicing the interest of the company and its shareholders.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">By filling an affidavit-in-opposition, the respondent nos. 2-6 contend that they are the shareholders and Directors of the company and, also, the partners of the newly-formed partnership business. The respondent nos. 2, 3 and 4 purchased portions of the 1<sup>st</sup> floor in 2017 and from November, 2017, they launched the restaurant business in the name of ‘Marine Drive Restaurant’ as per the decision taken in the 11<sup>th</sup> Board meeting. Being agitated with the activities of the mandatory signatory in payment of rent against their respective flats as well as the bills owed to the company (Neeshorgo Hotel and Resort Limited) against the services provided by the Marine Drive Restaurant, the respondent nos. 2-6 formed a Partnership Firm, namely, ‘Neeshorgo Management Enterprise’ to manage their flats. Thereafter, other flat-owners approached the respondent nos. 2-6 to rent out their flats through the Enterprise. Till date, the said agreements are being continued without any hindrance and the respondent nos. 2-6 have been paying rent to the flat-owners on a regular basis without any default. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">By filing a separate affidavit-in-opposition, the respondent nos. 11-48 state that the respondent nos. 11-48 are the flat owners of the building named ‘Neeshorgo’ at Plot no. 492, Kolatali Marine Drive Road, Cox’s Bazar. They have purchased their respective flats either from the landowner or from the Developer-company. They initially rented out their flats to the company, but the said company was very much irregular in payment of rents and in spite of repeated requests, the company was not paying monthly rents, resulting in financial loss of the respondent nos. 11-48. Under these circumstances, in order to minimize their loss, the flat-owners decided not to proceed any further in renting out the flats to the company and they decided to terminate their agreements to the company by issuing notice of termination. In the meantime, they came to know that the respondent nos. 2-6 have incorporated a Partnership Firm (the Enterprise) in the same building to manage their flats. On getting the above information, the respondent nos. 11-48 inquired about their business and came to know that the respondent nos. 2-6 are doing business with proper management, and being encouraged by, and on looking into, their business prospect and business activities, the respondent nos. 11-48 approached the respondent nos. 2-6 and they rented out their flats to the Enterprise vide separate rent agreements. After the respondents entered into new agreements with the Enterprise, they have been receiving their rents on a regular basis without any default. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the petitioners, Mr. Asif Bin Anwar submits that the respondent nos. 2-6 have admittedly put themselves in a position of conflict with the company inasmuch as the respondent nos. 2-6 being the shareholders and Directors of the company engaged themselves as the partners of the Enterprise to run a similar business in the same building, that is to say, in conducting hotel &amp; resort business at the same spot being Plot no. 492, Kolatoli, Marine Drive Road, Cox’s Bazar by damaging the business of the company. By placing the provisions of Article 23 of the AoA of the company, he submits that the respondent nos. 2-6<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>have committed a gross misconduct and have fallen within the scope of disqualification of Directors within the meaning of the said Article 23 of the AoA. He argues that since the respondent nos. 2-6 have put themselves in a position of conflict with the company, they have acted in contravention of their fiduciary duties. By placing the annexure-K series, the learned Advocate for the petitioners submits that the respondent nos. 2-6 have been in contravention of the fiduciay duty with the company by not only allowing the parallel business under the Partnership Firm (the Enterprise), but also by receiving the bills of the company, through the Credit Card Machine of the company’s rival business firm. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In support of his above count of submissions, the learned Advocate for the petitioners refers to the case of </span><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB;">Super-Max Offshore Holdings v Rakesh Malhotra, Actis Consumer Grooming Products Limited ([2017] EWHC 3246 (Comm) </span></em><span lang="EN-GB" style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-ansi-language: EN-GB;">and the case of<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"> Adesokan v Sainsbury's Supermarkets Ltd, ([2017] EWCA Civ 22</em></span><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">)</span></em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Asif Bin Anwar, the learned Advocate for the petitioners, then, draws the attention of this Court to the fact that since the petitioners and the respondent nos. 8 &amp; 9 have ensured that they shall not get involved in the business of the<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>Partnership Firm and they shall not do anything which may cause loss to the business of the company and, since both of them have agreed to accept the resolution dated 20.04.2018 taken in the EGM and since it has been amicably settled that they shall be performing the duty of the Directors towards helping the company, the petitioners are not seeking any relief against the respondent nos. 8 &amp; 9 and, accordingly, the learned Advocate for the petitioners makes a humble prayer that the prayer made against the respondent nos. 8 &amp; 9 in this petition as to removing them from the position of Directors of the company should be ignored. He contends that if the respondent nos. 2-6 refrain from damaging the business of the company by closing down the Partnership Firm in the same building, the petitioners shall not pray for their removal too. He further contends that since all the efforts of the petitioners are directed at rescuing the company from its death/annihilation, the petitioners are even ready to make any one out of the respondent nos. 2-6 either as the Chairman or as the Managing Director of the company, subject to the condition that they must be transparent to the other Directors in operating the Bank account and maintaining the accounts of the company and they shall also hold the AGM of the company regulary upon preparation of the Financial Reports of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. A.M. Aminuddin, the learned Senior Advocate, appearing for the respondent nos. 2-6 and also for the respondent nos. 11-48, contends that the deadlock in the company was created at the behest of a Director of the company, who is a retired Additional Chief Engineer against whom ACC has filed a criminal case for allegation of corruption during his service time in the Government offices. He further contends that from the date of the incorporation of the company, there is no activity of the company, nor does this company possess any property. He contends that, in fact, the company currently exists only in the papers, as most of the flat owners have disassociated themselves from the company. He, then, sought permission to allow him to leave the Court with a prayer to permit his juniors Mr. Sakib Rejwan Kabir and Md. Minhaduzzaman to make submissions on behalf of the respondent nos. 2-6 &amp; 11-48. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Sakib Rejwan Kabir, appearing on behalf of the respondent nos. 2-6, submits that since the allegations raised by the petitioners are not in relation to any action of majority against the interest of the company and since there is no precise allegation that the action of the majority as a whole is prejudicial to the interest of the minority shareholders, the dispute does not come within the ambit of Section 233 of the Companies Act. He next submits that since the petitioners have raised disputed questions of fact, their adjudication requires taking oral evidence in a properly framed suit, and not in the present proceedings under Section 233 of the Companies Act and, therefore, the present application under Section 233 of the Companies Act is not maintainable. On this issue, he further submits that the cancellation of contracts with the company and execution of fresh agreements of the flats with the Enterprise by the flat owners in respect of management of the apartments are all matters of Civil Court to adjudicate upon. He next submits that the respondent nos. 2-6 did not violate Article 23 of the AoA of the company as they have not done anything which goes against the interest of the company, because the rent agreements of the flat owners have been terminated much earlier than the date when respondent nos. 2-6 entered into agreements with the flat owners and had the respondent nos. 2-6 not executed the rent agreements, the flat owners would have rented out their flats to third parties and as such the petitioners could not be removed from their position as Directors of the company. The learned Advocate for the respondent nos. 2-6 submits that the allegation brought against these respondents do not fall within the definition of gross misconduct and, therefore, they should not be debarred from performing the duty as the Directors of the company. He lastly submits that since all the flat owners of the ‘Neeshorgo’ have pulled themselves out of the company, the company is no more in existence and, on the other hand, since they have joined the Enterprise, it should be declared as a valid business. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Md. Minhaduzzaman, the learned Advocate appearing on behalf of the respondent nos. 11-48, contends that these respondents have already cut off their contractual relationship with the company, as they were not getting rents regularly. He further contends that these respondents have entered into contracts with the newly formed Partnership Firm under the name and style of Neeshorgo Management Enterprise and they are happy to have their agreement continued with this newly created Enterprise. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The learned Advocate for the respondent nos. 8 &amp; 9 (who are the petitioners of the Company Matter No. 151 of 2018) contends that they are not involved in any manner with the formation of the separate Partnership Firm and they shall be the happiest persons to see that the company is running smoothly and making profit. He submits that since the prayer of these respondents as to amicably settling the dispute between these two respondents and the petitioners has been allowed by this Court, these respondents are not contesting this matter. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Upon perusing the petitions of both the Company Matters, affidavits-in-opposition and the annexed papers as well as after hearing the learned Advocates for all the parties to these two Company Matters, it appears to me that on the Plot No. 492, Kalatoli, Marine Drive Road, Cox’s Bazar, a 10-storied mega building containing about 100 flats and 1(one) open space at the first floor have been constructed by Khetra Architects and Engineers Ltd (the Developer-company). This iconic plaza has been named ‘Neeshorgo’ by the Developer-company. The petitioners and all the respondents are the owners of the flats of the ‘Neeshorgo’. They have purchased their flats either from the land owner’s portion of 60% or from the Developer-company’s portion of 40% and, still now, the land owner and the Developer-company own some open spaces/flats, including the open space at first floor which is now being used as the restaurant (Marine Drive Restaurant), even after selling out the significant number of flats from their respective portions. The Managing Director and the Chairman of the Developer-company, eventually in the year 2016, came out with an idea that the flats and the restaurant may be rented out to a company with a view to getting the rents of the flats and restaurant without any hassle. Although it was possible to rent the flats to one company/individual, and the restaurant to a separate company/individual, they decided to manage all these assets by one company and, for the aforesaid purpose, most of the flat owners and owners of the restaurant-space at first floor (who are the Managing Director and Chairman of the Developer-company) formed a company having it incorporated as the ‘Neeshorgo Hotel and Resort Ltd’ on 27.01.2016. Thus, it appears to me that the company is not the owner of any flat or open space of this plaza named ‘Neeshorgo’. The company has simply taken lease/rent of the spaces/flats of this building. From the Memorandum of Association and Articles of Assocaition of the company, it transpires that the aim and object of the company is to run hotel and resort business, either by purchasing the flats, open space or by taking rent from the flat owners and building owners not only of this single premise (the Neeshorgo), but by purchasing and taking rent of other properties from all over Bangladesh and, simultaneously, to expand the business outside Bangladesh. In other words, the object of the company is not to keep its activities limited only within the periphery of a single spot at the Plot No. 492, Kolatoli, Marine Drive Road, Cox’s Bazar, but also to spread its business in some other suitable places of Bangladesh and abroad.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Apparently, it was a noble initiative by the Managing Director and the Chairman of the Developer-company to show the flat owners a dream of making them the owners/shareholders of an incorporated company, in addition to getting rent of their respective flats and space and also to enjoy dividends, if the company flourishes. In other words, the flat owners who would become the shareholders of the company would hold two statuses, and financially they would be benefitted in two ways. Their first status is that they are the flat/space owners of the plaza named ‘Neeshorgo’ and their second status is that they are the owners of a company engaged in hotel and resort business named ‘Neeshorgo Hotel and Resort Ltd’. And, from the perspective of financial benefit, while on the one hand, they shall get rent of their respective flats/spaces from the company, on the other hand, if the company can make profit, they would get dividends. Thus, the flat owners of this edifice ‘Neeshorgo’ hold separate and distinct entity from having their entity as the shareholders of the company (Neeshogro Hotel and Resort Ltd). While the flat owners who have not become the shareholders of the company are free to rent out their flats either to the company or to any person or they themselves may live therein, similarly, the flat owners who have become the shareholders of the company are also at liberty to rent out their respective flats either to their company or to other person/company or they themselves may stay therein and if the shareholder-cum-flat owners rent out the flats to the company, they will get the rents for the flats like the other general flat owners. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">So, whether the flat owners would rent out their flats to the company or to the newly formed Partnership Firm or they themselves would manage their flats/space is a matter, out of the touch and reach of this Company Matter No. 295 of 2018. Therefore, the flat owners who are not the shareholders of the company, such as the respondent nos. 11-48, have nothing to do in these cases, and the petitioners rightly had not impleaded them as the respondents of this Company Matter. But, for the reason best known to them, they filed an application for addition of party in this Company Matter No. 295 of 2018. Although this Court was reluctant to allow their application for addition of party, however, on the persistent insistence of the learned Advocates for the respondent nos. 2-6 &amp; 11-48, they were added as the proper party; not as the necessary party. However, had the application for addition of party been strictly considered by this Court, their status would have been found to be one, which does not even come within the ambit of the proper party. But, since there was a direction by the Hon’ble Appellate Division upon this Court to give final verdicts on these two Company Matters (Company Matter No. 151 of 2019 and Company Matter No. 295 of 2019) on or before 09.05.2019, this Court considered it prudent not to create an opportunity for the respondents of the Company Matter No. 295 of 2019 to take the matter again before the Appellate Division against the Order of rejection of their application for addition of party towards squandering further time in disposing of two substantive Company Matters.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the light of the position of the added respondent nos. 11-48 that, as the flat owners of this mega building, they are always at liberty either to live in their respective flats or to rent out to the company or to rent out to the newly formed Partneship Firm or to any other individual or proprietorship businesses or partnership business or company and, further, given the nature of their legal relationship with the petitioners, the issue as to whether they are still with the company or they have terminated their contracts with the company, or whether they are currently with the newly formed Partnership Firm, is not the subject matter of the present application under Section 233 of the Companies Act. Therefore, I do not find any issue to be framed and adjudicated upon by this Court for the respondent nos. 11-48. More importantly, since the petitioners have neither sought any relief against the respondents nor have the petitioners brought any allegation against them in the petition, there is no issue to be framed for adjudicaton, so far as the respondent nos. 11-48 are concerned. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">And, since the respondent nos. 8 &amp; 9 (who are the Chairman and the Managing Director of the company and the petitioners of the Company Matter No. 151 of 2018) have already settled their dispute amicably with the petitioners, there is no issue to be framed for adjudication in this case. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Therefore, the only contesting respondents remain in this case are the respondent nos. 2-6. With this scenario, this Court is now obligated to frame the issues as to whether the attachment of the respondent nos. 2-6 in the company as the Directors of this company is beneficial or pre-judicial to the interest of this company and, secondly, whether this Court should make any declaration as to the legality of forming the Partnership Firm or as to the existence of the company. However, since the learned Advocates for the respondent nos. 2-6 have raised the issue of maintainability of this petition, let me embark upon the said issue at first. For examining the maintainability issue, it would be profitable to quote the provisions of Section 233 of the Companies Act, which run as follows:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">233. Power of Court to give direction for protecting interest of the minority</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">:- (1) Subject to the fulfilment of the conditions of the required minimum as specified in Section 195(a) and 195(b) <u>any member</u> or debenture holder of a company <u>may</u> either individually or jointly <u>bring to the notice of the court</u> by application that- </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">(a)  <u>the affairs of the company are being conducted or the powers of the directors are being exercised in a manner prejudicial to one or more of its members or debenture </u></span><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">holders or in disregard of his or their interest</span></u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">, or </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(b)<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>the company is acting or is likely to act in a manner which discriminated or is likely to discriminate the interest of any member or debenture holder;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt;">(c)<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">  </span>a resolution of the members, debenture holders or any class of them has been passed or is likely to be passed which discriminates or is likely to discriminate the interest of one or more of the members or likely to debenture holder; </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">and pray for such order, as in his or their opinion, would be necessary for safeguarding his or their interest and also the interest of any other member</span></u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> or debenture holder. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(2) <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>The Court shall, on receipt of an application under sub-section (1) send a copy thereof to the Board and fix a date for hearing the application. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(3) <span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span><u>If after hearing the parties present on the date so fixed, the Court is of opinion that the interest of the applicant or applicants has been or is being or is likely to be prejudicially affected for reasons specified in the application, it may make such order as prayed for or such other order as it deems fit including a direction</u>-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(a) to cancel or modify any resolution or transaction; </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(b) to regulate the conduct of the company's affairs in future in such manner as is specified therein. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(c) to amend any provision of the memorandum and articles of the company (underlined by me).</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">From a plain perusal of the above provisions of law, it appears to me that while sub-Section (1) of Section 233 of the Companies Act stipulates the qualifications required for a person in order to become an applicant of a Section-233 application, clauses (a) to (c) of the said sub-Section (1) provides the issues/subjects/grievances which may be brought to the notice of the Company Court, and at the end of sub-Section (1) of Section 233 of the Companies Act, the Legislature endows the applicant with wide options of making prayers to the Company Court. Then, sub-Section (3) of Section-233 of the Companies Act speaks about the role and power of the Company Court in disposing of a Section-233 application.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">About the petitioners’ qualification/ competency to stand as the applicant of a Section-233 application, since no question has been raised by the respondents, this Court is not going to embark upon examination of the aforesaid aspect. However, it may be briefly stated here that since the petitioners collectively hold 33.33% of the total issued shares, they are well competent to stand as the petitioners of a Section-233 application. Apparently, the respondent nos. 2-6 have raised the maintainability issue on the grounds that (i) no specific allegation has been brought against them, (ii) whatever the allegations they have brought, those can not be resolved in the Company Bench, for, oral evidence would require adjudication of the allegations and (iii) the issue as to whether the contracts of the respondent nos. 11 to 48 with the company have been terminated or not, can not be adjudicated upon in a Company Matter. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Let me see whether there is substance in the aforesaid arguments made by the learned Advocates for the respondent nos. 2-6 on the ground of maintainability of the Company Matter No. 295 of 2018. The first ground is that no specific allegation has been brought by the petitioners against the respondents (the majority shareholders).
