In the light of the admitted fact that since the respondent nos. 2-6 &amp; 8-9 collectively are the majority shareholders, and since the respondent nos. 8 &amp; 9 as the Managing Director &amp; the Chairman and the respondent nos. 2-6 as the Directors of the company were not taking necessary steps for conducting the audit of the company, nor were they holding the AGM of the company, and since all of the respondent nos. 2-6 directly and the respondent nos. 8 &amp; 9 as abettors were blamed to have formed a parallel rival business, there is no scope for the respondents to say that no specific allegation has been brought against them. As per clause (a) of Section 233 (1) of the Companies Act, the petitioners are simply required to bring to the notice of this Court that <span style="mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">the affairs of the company are being conducted or the powers of the directors are being exercised in a manner prejudicial to one or more of its members or debenture </span>holders or in disregard of his or their interest. From the above admitted facts as to not conducting the audit of the company and non-holding of the AGMs of the company, it is vividly evident that <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">‘the affairs of the company are being conducted ……….. in a manner prejudicial to one on more of its members’</em> and, thus, I find that the petitioners having flawlessly brought to the notice of this Court the said admitted affairs of the company in a specific manner, there is no scope for the respondents to question the maintainability of this petition on the ground that no specific allegation has been brought against the respondents. In other words, while the petitioners have perfectly satisfied this Court about the requirement of Section 233(1)(a) of the Companies Act, the submissions of the learned Advocate for the respondent nos. 2-6 have no legs to stand upon and, accordingly, the same are repelled by the Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Although there are some other allegations of not running the affairs of the company in a beneficial manner (a) by not operating the Bank account with the signatures of the authorized Directors, (b) by running a parallel rivalry business at the same site, (c) by not signing the further agreements with the flat owners, (d) by not paying the rents to the flat owners regularly and so on, however, I would not go for examination of each of the aforesaid allegations, for, when the allegations of not conducting the audit and not holding the AGM are the admitted facts by all the respondents, and the allegation of commencing a new parallel business is also admitted by the respondent nos. 2-6, which sufficientty attracts the provisions of clause (a) of Section 233 (1) of the Companies Act, there is no need to deal with other factual issues by this Court. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The second ground of maintainability is that this Court is legally not empowered to adjudicate upon the factual issues involved in this case. There are two types of factual issues in any case, namely, admitted facts and disputed facts. When the facts contended by the plaintiff/petitioner are admitted by the defendants/respondents, question of taking any oral or documentary evidence becomes redundant. And, if any fact stated by the petitioner is disputed, not only by raising mere objection but also by attempting to substantiate the objection through credible written statements/affidavit and upon adducing the relevant document/paper, if any, in that scenario, the Courts are required to take oral evidence in an effort to discover and assess the truth. Now, the pertinent question that crops up for consideration is whether this Court is empowered to take oral evidence, if needed, for finding out the truth to arrive at the appropriate conclusion. In reply thereto, my humble understanding of the scheme of the Companies Act is that the Legislature intended to<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>resolve all types of disputes or grievances arising out of the Companies Act expeditiously through a higher rank of Court i. e. either the District Court or the High Court Division, in a summary manner so as to help smoothly flourish the business and commerce without experiencing protracted, time-consuming and complex procedures which are required to be followed/observed/applied by the Civil Courts and, therefore, most of the Company Matters relating to/arising out of/in connection with the grievance of any members of the company or debenture holder of the company are tried/adjudicated upon without taking any oral evidence. However, it does not necessarily mean that the Company Court is not competent to dispose of a company case by taking oral evidance, because there is no provision within the four corners of the Companies Act prohibiting the Company Court to take oral evidence. Rather, the expressions employed in Section 233(3) of the Companies Act, <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“If after hearing the parties present on the date……”,</em> implies that there may be petitioner witness/es (PW/s) or respondent witness/es (RW/s) or the Court witnesses/es (CW/s) if the facts and circumstances so warrant, inasmuch as this Court requires to form an opinion <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“If the Court is of the opinion”, </em>(the wordings of Section 233 (3) of the Companies Act) for passing necessary Order and/or Direction. Thus, I hold that since the Company Court is competent to frame any issue for trial, any complicated question of facts can be adjudicated upon by it through taking documentary and oral evidence towards passing an appropriate Order and Direction. Therefore, the ground taken by the learned Advocates for the respondents gets repelled. Even for the sake of argument if it is held, without being prejudiced, that the Company Court does not have the power to adjudicate upon the cases by taking oral evidence, in that event also, the ground taken by the learned Advocate for the respondents will not stand, for, the allegations of (i) not conducting the audit of the company, (ii) not holding the AGM of the company and (iii) running a rival business in the same building being admitted facts, there is no need of taking any oral evidence on these factual issues. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The last ground is that, since the issue as to whether valid contracts exist between the company and the flat owners can not be adjudicated upon here in this case, the petition under Section 233 of the Companies Act is not maintainable. This Court is fully in agreement with the above proposition. This Court’s clear opinion is that whether the respondent nos. 2-6 or 11-48 have got any contractual relationship with the company as the tenant and landlord, is a matter to be adjudicated upon by the Civil Court. Given the fact that the petitioners have not sought for adjudication of an issue of this sort here in this Company Matter, therefore, I find it to be a completely irrelevant ground for attacking this case, on the issue of maintainability of this case. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">34.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The above examen on the issue of maintainability of this application under Section 233 of the Companies Act leads me to hold that there is no substance in the arguments advanced by the learned Advocate for the respondent nos. 2-6 for rejection of this application on the ground of maintainability of this application under Section 233 of the Companies Act.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">35.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now, let me take up the substantive issue as to whether the respondent nos. 2-6 deserve to remain as the Directors of the company. To delve deep into this issue, it would be useful if I may know the statutory and dictionary meanings of a Director of a company. Section 2(1)(f) of Companies Act defines the word ‘Director’ in the following manner; </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.25in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Section 2(1)(f): </span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“Director” includes any person occupying the position of director by whatever name called;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">36.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The above provision of law does not provide the definitive meaning of the word “Director” and, therefore, I need to take recourse to a dictionary to know the proper meaning of the word ‘Director’. Black’s Law Dictionary inscribes the following narration about the word ‘Director’ which is quoted below: </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.25in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“A person appointed or elected to sit on a Board that manages the affairs of a corporation or other organization by electing and exercising control over its officers. Also, trustee.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">37.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Sections 90 to 110 of the Companies Act set out the provisions on the different aspects of the Directors of an incorporated company, including appointment of Directors (Section 91), disqualifications of Directors (Section 94), qualification of a Director (Section 97), removal of Directors (Section 106) and vacation of office of Directors (Section 108). From a minute perusal of the entire provisions relating to Directors in the Companies Act, as enshrined in Sections 90 to 110, my humble understanding about the terminology “Director” is that a Director is a person who is elected by the majority members entrusting upon him/her day-to-day business activities and finances and, also, to ensure that all statutory filing obligations are met. Thus, the Directors of the company in true sense are the ‘trustees’ of the company as defined in the Black’s Law Dictionary. The shareholders /members of the company keep a trust upon the Directors that they shall do everything for the welfare and benefit of the company and its members and, therefore, there exists a fiduciary relationship between the Directors and others members of the company. Once this fiduciary relationship is broken, a Director must no longer hold the position of a Director of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">38.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Having laid down the above dictum on the term “Director”, I need to see now whether the respondent nos. 2-6 have lost the trust of the shareholders (members) of the company resulting in breaking up the fiduciary relationship between them.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">         </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">39.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is an admitted fact that the respondent nos. 2-6 have created a Partnership Firm under the name and style of ‘Neeshorgo Management Enterprise’ which has been impleaded in this petition as respondent no.7. It is also an admitted position that the respondent nos. 2-6 while performing functions as the Directors of this company did not take any consent from the company to form another parallel business during the existence of this company. If the respondent nos. 2-6 were eager to run a separate business of the same nature at the same spot under the same roof, it was the duty of these Directors of this company to, at least, discuss the issue in the Board meeting, let alone taking approval from the Board of the company and, thereafter, they could have opted to undertake a separate business under the same roof. Anyone with ordinary prudence would be of the view that if a parallel business is run under the same roof by the Directors of the existing company, the interest of the company as well as its shareholders would inevitably be jeopardised. And, particularly when it is admitted by these respondents that due to providing a better service by their newly formed Enterprise, the flat owners of the plaza ‘Neeshorgo’ are becoming interested to sever their ties with the company, it is crystal clear to this Court that the activities of the respondent nos. 2-6 are crippling the business of the company and, hence, there is no reason for the members of the company to trust them any longer as the trustees (Directors) of the company. Therefore, this Court is of the view that the respondent nos. 2-6, having acted against the interest of the company as well as the interest of the shareholders of the company, are not competent to perform their duty as the Directors of the company. In augmenting my above conclusion, I find it pertinent to state that when the majority members of a cricket team lose faith in some players because of the latter’s involvment in “match fixing” to help win the opponent team, like the respondent nos. 2-6, they should not be in the team any longer. Likewise, when an ocean-going ship is drifting in the middle of the sea and, eventually upon finding another boat/ship, a few of crew members selfishly escape by boarding therein, they lose their right to remain as the crew member of the ship.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">40.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now, a pertinent question may crop up as to under what provisions of law this Court is going to declare these Directors incompetent and expel them from the Board of Directors of the company. The answer thereto is that when the Court is of the opinion that the interest of the petitioner of a Section-233 application is being prejudicially affected, it may pass any Order it deems fit, as mandated by the Legislature in Section 233(3) of the Companies Act. Accordingly, in exercising the power vested in this Court under Section 233(3) of the Companies Act, this Court is well empowered to pass an Order decreeing that the respondent nos. 2-6 are hereby declared to be ‘disqualified’ or the offices of the respondent nos. 2-6 are hereby declared to have been ‘vacated’, but, for the reasons to be known hereinafter, I prefer not to use the legal terminologies ‘disqualified’ or ‘vacated’ in declaring them incompetent to be the members of the Board of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">41.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>However, because of not using the above-mentioned terminologies, there should not be any confusion that this Court can not declare any Director of the company to be ‘disqualified’ until a Director’s case falls within the ambit of Section 94 of the Companies Act or the office of a Director shall not be ‘vacated’ until a Director’s circumstance attracts the provisions of Section 108 of the Companies Act or a Director cannot be ‘removed’ without passing an extraordinary resolution under Section 106 of the Companies Act, inasmuch as the powers invested in the Court under Section 233(3) of the Companies Act is wider and superior than the power given to the Court by any other provisions of the Companies Act. By virtue of the power under Section 233(3) of the Companies Act, the Court is competent to order the company to conduct its audit, to appoint an Independent Auditor and to fix the remuneration of the Auditor, to direct the company for calling and holding any meeting (which may be Board meeting, EGM or AGM) and to make any necessary Order/Directions <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">‘to regulate the conduct of the company’s affairs’</em> (the expression engraved in Section 233(3)(b) of the Companies Act). However, since the power invested in this Court under Section 233(3) of the Companies Act is discretionary in nature, it should be exercised by this Court judiciously in the rarest of rare cases only upon carrying out meticulous examination of the facts and circumstance of an application under Section 233 of the Companies Act.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">42.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">I find this case to be a fit one to exercise the power under Section 233(3) of the Companies Act and, accordingly, I am inclined to declare the respondent nos. 2-6 of the Company Matter No. 295 of 2018 to be incompetent to be or to remain as the Directors of the company and, accordingly, the respondent nos. 2-6 are hereby declared to be incompetent to remain as the Directors of the company. In order to let the company run smoothly and more beneficially, this Court should expel the respondent nos. 2-6 from the Board of the company. Now, let me consider as to whether the respondent nos. 2-6 should be expelled straightaway from the Board of Directors by this Judgment now, or should they be given an opportunity to correct themselves.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">43.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">After declaring the respondent nos. 2-6 to be incompetent to be in the Board of the company, as a logical sequence, this Court should make the consequential Order of expelling the respondents from the Board. However, in my view, it would be a prudent exercise if this Court gives these respondents an opportunity to think over their actions so far taken by them in running a rivalry business and consider as to whether they can unitedly run the company, like the respondent nos. 8 &amp; 9, in a dream of making the company a reputed chain Hotel and Resort Company. For this to happen, the declaration made by this Court hereinbefore as to becoming or remaining incompetent as the Directors of the company is temporarily kept in abeyance till the date of holding the first Board meeting of the company, in an expectation by this Court that the respondent nos. 2-6 upon attending the Board meeting of the company will inform the Board about the closure of their Enterprise. If they do not turn up in the aforesaid Board meeting or if they do not agree to shut down the Enterprise, the company shall be competent to remove them from their directorship under Section 106 of the Companies Act. A company is competent to remove any of its shareholder-Directors under Section 106 of the Companies Act showing him as disqualified under Section 94 of the Companies Act or declaring the Director’s seat to have fallen vacant under Section 108 of the Companies Act. From a mere perusal of the provisions of Article 23(f) of the AoA of the company that <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“The office of the Directors shall be vacated…. for any work against the interest of the company”</em>, it appears to me that the aforesaid provision in an unambiguous term empowers the company to declare vocation of the seats of the respondent nos. 2-6 as the Directors of the company, as they have been found by this Court to have worked against the interest of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">44.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In addition to the above provisions, to put the company on a safer side for endowing the company with a more specific power for removing these respondents, if needed, under Section 108 of the Companies Act, this Court is inclined to exercise its power under Section 233(3)(1) of the Companies Act towards directing the company to amend its Articles of Association to incorporate a provision as Article No. 23(g), which shall be added at the end of Article No. 23 and be placed as sub-Article (g) after the sub-Article (f) of Article No. 23. The following wordings shall be incorporated<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">“runs any Hotel and Restaurant business anywhere in the world without the approval of the company”</em> as a disqualification for appointment of a Director. An incorporated company is competent to insert in its Articles of Association any provisions of disqualification in the matter of becoming a Director by virtue of the company’s power given in Section 94(2) of the Companies Act, in addition to the provisions relating to disqualifications for the Directors set out in Section 94(1) of the Companies Act. Also, under Section 108(2) of the Companies Act, a company is empowered to incorporate other provisions as the grounds for vacating the office of the Directors provided in Section 108(1) of the Companies Act. Once the company amends its Article 23 in the manner as prescribed above, it may apply the said provision for vacation of the office of the respondent nos. 2-6, if they are not volitional to leave off their Enterprise. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">45.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now, I need to take up the second substantive issue as to whether this Court should make any declaration as to the legality of forming the Partnership Firm or as to the existence of the company. Mr. Sakib, the learned Advocate for the respondent nos. 2-6, has submitted that since all the flat owners of the ‘Neeshorgo’ have pulled themselves out of the company, the company is no more in existence and, on the other hand, since they have joined the Enterprise, it should be declared as a valid business. From a careful reading of all the prayers made in this case, I did not find any prayer seeking a declaration that formation of the Partnership Firm named ‘Neeshorgo Management Enterprise’ was illegal. From a plain perusal of the entire petition in tandem with its prayers, I find that the petitioners’ case is not at all directed at obtaining such a declaration.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">46.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. AM Aminuddin, the learned Senior Counsel, has submitted that since the company does not run practically, there is no point of allowing the petitioners to operate the business of the company. On this issue, this Court’s view is that until and unless the company is dissolved through the process of winding up, there is no impediment for the company to carry out its business in full swing. The incident of opening up a new business by the influential Directors of the company or the whimsical decision of some landlords as to deserting the company or the financial stutus of the company as to not possessing any fund - can not lead this Court to go for a declaration that the company does no more exist, in this application under Section 233 of the Companies Act. So, this Court is neither going to declare the ‘Neeshorgo Management Enterprise’ as an illegal business nor going to declare that the company has lost its substratum necessitating its dissolution. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">47.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The above proposition, now, leads me to embark upon the issue as to whether this Court should make appopropriate Observations, Orders and Directions for this company, so that it may unhesitatingly go for its next course of actions, particularly, in the backdrop of keeping the existence of both these two business entities intact by this Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">48.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It is to be known, if it is already not known, that the Company Court acts as the ‘Ombudsman’ of the companies; meaning that normally the Company Court will not interfere with the internal affairs of the company, but if the situation demands, then the Court shall do the needful. While only in a few circumstances, this Court is competent to <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suo motu</em> interfere with the management of the company, however, in most of the events, this Court is allowed to look into the affairs of the company upon receiving an application. This is the scheme of enactment of Company Laws in most of the countries around the world. In other words, any action taken or omissions occured either by the member/s of the Board (such as, Director, Managing Director and Chairman) or by the agent/s of the company (such as, Company Secretary, General Manager, Accounts Officer and other Officers) in running/managing the affairs of the company, may be examined by this Court either <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suo motu</em> or on receiving application. For example, the Legislature has vested the power in this Court to <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suo motu</em> direct the company to call, hold and conduct any meeting (Board Meeting, Extraordinary General Meeting, Annual General Meeting) when the situation described in Section 85(3) so warrants and, in dealing with the above situation, the Company Court is also empowered to pass any ancilliary, consequential and supplementary Order and Directions, including passing Order for appointment of auditor, fixing its remuneration, etc. It was held in the case of Md. M. Rahman Vs Joint Stock Companies 2019(1) 15 ALR 96 that this Court is empowered to <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">suo motu</em> direct the company under Section 85(3) of the Companies Act to hold AGM/s of the company and to pass any other Order and Direction which may be considered by the Court to be necessary.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">49.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Similarly, in an application under Section 233 of the Companies Act this Court is empowered to pass any type of Order/Direction which the Court considers to be necessary for the betterment of the company. Although there are differences of opinion as to the jurisdiction of this Court that the jurisdiction of this Court is limited within the certain provisions of the Companies Act, where the said provisions prescribe the petitioner/aggrieved person for approaching the Company Court (such as Sections 12, 13, 14, 41, 43, 59, 71, 81, 82, 83, 85, 115, 151, 171, 175, 176, 191, 193, 228, 229, 233, 241, 245, 248, 249, 253, 255, 258, 259, 261, 262, 263, 264, 265, 267-286, 294, 296, 299, 300, 301, 302, 303, 305, 309, 311, 312, 314, 316, 326, 328, 331, 333, 338, 339, 340, 342, 346, 349, 395, 396),<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>however, upon minute perusal of the Preamble and the entire provisions of the Companies Act, my view is that in the absence of any prohibitory provision in any Section of the Companies Act, in particular in Section 3 of the Companies Act which seeks to state about the jurisdiction of this Court, this Court is competent to deal with any issues/grievance relating to or arising out of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>or in connection with any provisions of the Companies Act.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">50.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In any event, this Court being well-empowered to pass necessary Orders and/or Directions and Observations in an application under Section 233 of the Companies Act, I consider it to be useful to make the following Observations, Orders and Directions for the company;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Orders, Directions and Observations for Company Matter No. 151 of 2018;</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(1)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The resolutions taken in the EGM dated 20.04.2018 are valid. The founding Chairman and the founding Managing Director of the company shall perform the duties as Directors of the company. The present Chairman and Managing Director of the company shall be appointed as per the resolution taken in the EGM held on 20.04.2018, subject to the outcome of the first Board meeting to be held under the neutral Chairman to be appointed by this Court hereinafter.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(2)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Order of stay granted earlier at the time of admission of this matter staying the operation of the resolution dated 20.04.2018, is hereby recalled and vacated. The company and its Chairman, Managing Director and other Directors are directed to operate the Bank accounts of the company under the signatures of the newly appointed Chairman and Managing Director, subject to the decision taken in the first Board meeting to be held under the leadership of the Court-appointed Chairman. However, the company shall be at liberty to make another signatory from the other Directors in consonance with the scheme of resolution taken in the 10<sup>th</sup> Board Meeting of the company. In any event, they shall always keep the founding Chairman and the founding Managing Director of the company updated with the status of accounts of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(3)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">With the above Observations, Directions and Orders, the Company Matter No. 151 of 2018 is disposed of, however, without any order as to costs. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Orders, Directions and Observations for Company Matter No. 295 of 2018;</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(1)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The company is directed to notify the Registrar of Joint Stock Companies &amp; Firms about the amendment of the AoA made by this Court hereinbefore, within fourteen days from the date of receiving this Judgment.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(2)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The respondent nos. 2-6 are declared incompetent to remain in the post of the Directors of this company. But they are not removed/expelled from the Board for now.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(3)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The newly appointed Chairman and the Managing Director of the company either themselves or with the assistance of the founding Chairman and the founding Managing Director shall invite the respondent nos. 2-6 to attend the first Board meeting to be held under the chairmanship of the Court-appointed neutral Chairman, in addition to sending letters by registered posts, e-Mails and by fax to their latest addresses by the Company Secretary, at the instance of the Court-appointed Chairman. They shall put their best efforts to ensure attendance/presence of all the Directors of the company. Presence of the respondent nos. 2-6 and the founding Chairman and the founding Managing Director in the aforfesaid Board meeting is specifically and notably expected by this Court.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(4)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the aforesaid meeting, if the respondent nos. 2-6 turn up, the newly appointed Chairman and the Managing Director together with the founding Chairman and the founding Managing Director shall endeavour to pursue them to close down the new business of the respondent nos. 2-6. If the respondents are found to be adamant to run the new business, they shall be removed from the position of the Directors of the company upon taking a resolution to that effect invoking Section 106 of the Companies Act.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(5)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">If the respondent nos. 2-6 agree in the aforesaid meeting to shut down the partnership business, the findings of this Court about the respondent nos. 2-6 as to being incompetent to remain as the Directors of the company shall be ineffective and, accordingly, all of respondent nos. 2-6 shall remain as the Directors of the company. And out of the respondent nos. 2-6, at least, one shall be appointed the Chairman or the Managing Director of the company. However, the Board shall be free to offer them both the posts aiming at keeping the respondent nos. 2-6 in the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(6)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. AM Aminuddin, who is not only a Senior Advocate of this Court but also the President of the Supreme Court Bar Association, has brought an issue to the notice of the Court that because of a Director of the company (who is the retired Additional Chief Engineer of the Roads and Highways and against whom ACC is carrying out investigation of alleged corruption), division among the Directors has been created. Therefore, this Court directs the company not to keep or include him in the Board of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(7)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Khan Mohammad Shameem Aziz, Bar-at-Law (Mobile: 01713-048450), an Advocate of the Appellate Division of the Supreme Court of Bangladesh, is hereby appointed as the Chairman of the company only for specific purpose to be stated hereinafter. He shall preside over the company’s Board Meeting to be held within 90 days from the date of receipt of this Judgement and Order. The company shall pay a sum of Taka 5,00,000/- (five lacs) as his remuneration. The learned Advocates for both the sides are hereby directed to notify their respective parties that the Board meeting shall be held either at the company’s registered address or at the place to be agreed upon by them. The quorum of the Board meeting shall be as per the provisions of the AoA of the company. However the Court-appointed Chairman shall put his best effort to ensure attendance of 1 (one) Director from the group of the petitioners, 1 (one) Director from the group of the respondent nos. 2-6 and 1 (one) Director from the founding Chairman and the Managing Director in the Board meeting.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The newly appointed Chairman and the Managing Director of the company and the founding Chairman and the founding Managing Director of the company are directed to immediately contact the Court-appointed Chairman and furnish him the latest Mobile Numbers, e-Mail addresses and postal addresses of all the 21 Directors of the company within 1 (one) week of receiving this Judgment. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Court-appointed Chairman is directed to sit with the Court-appointed Independent Auditor (CA Firm) and the Board of Directors of the company within 2(two) weeks from the date of recipet of this Judgment and Order and take necessary steps for scheduling the dates of the AGMs of the company.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; The company shall pay a consolidated fee of Taka 3,00,000/- (three lacs) to the appointed CA Firm.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(11)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The CA Firm is directed to contact the present Chairman and the Managing Director of the company and to remain present in the Board meeting to be held within two weeks and, thereby, commence the audit work.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(12)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The above-named CA Firm is directed to figure out the (i) assets, (ii) liabilities and (iii) balance of the company. In carrying out the above task, the auditing firm shall be at liberty to look into and touch upon any subjects, which are usually done by any professional auditor.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(13)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The audit firm is hereby directed to submit their audit report to the Court-appointed Chairman within 60 (sixty) days from the date of having their consolidated fees. The company, the present Chairman, the Managing Director, the founding Chairman, the founding Managing Director and all other Directors of the company, including the respondent nos. 2-6, are hereby directed to effectively assist the Court-appointed Auditor in conducting the audit of the company within the prescribed time.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(14)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The Court-appointed Chairman is directed to call, hold and conduct all the AGMs of the company under his chairmanship either at the registered address of the company or at his chosen place and, thereafter, file before this Court an affidavit containing a report on the activities carried out and the businesses transacted by him in the Board meeting, AGMs and about other dealings/interactions with the Directors of the company. The affidavit must state (i) whether the company has notified the RJSC about the amendment of the AoA, (ii) whether the respondent nos. 2-6 and the founding Chairman and Directors had attended the Board meeting and (iii) it also state about other business transactions during his chairmanship, in addition to annexing a report on the minutes of Board meetings and the AGMs.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo3; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 81.0pt;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(15)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The fees of the Court-appointed Chairman, the costs of conducting the audit, the money for donation and any other incidental expenses, if incurred, will be borne by the company. In the event that there is no fund available in the account of the company or delay occurs to have access to the fund of the company, the petitioners of Company Matter No. 295 of 2018 shall lend the required amount of money to the company and, later on, they shall be entitled to the reimbursment of the same from the company.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">51.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">This Judgment and Order shall be effective subject to compliance of the directions, given hereinafter, as regards the donation. The Company will donate Tk. 2,00,000 (two lacs) only through Pay Order out of which (1) Tk. 1,00,000/- (one lac) to Anujani Zame Masjid and Pathagar Chatak, Sunamgonj, (2) Tk. 50,000/- (fifty thousand) to Baba Hazrat Ibrahim (A.) Jame Masjid, Comilla Sadar, Comilla and (3) Tk. 50,000/- (fifty thousand) to Khamargaon Khan Bari Masjid, Nandail, Mymenshing. On furnishing receipts of payment, this Order may be drawn up, if so prayed for.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l1 level1 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><!-- [if !supportLists]--><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">52.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><!--[endif]--><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-size: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Let a copy of this Judgment and Order be sent to the Registrar of Joint Stock Companies and Firms, Dhaka for information and necessary action.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Ed. </span></strong></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><!-- [if !supportFootnotes]--><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><!--[endif]--><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_November_19(2)/Issue%20__November__19(2)__Com.%20Mat.%20_295_151%20of%2018_M.%20Khurshid%20Alam%20Sarker,%20J.__2.doc#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 10.0pt; 814	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Md. Elias Vs.  The Commissioner of Taxes, Narayangonj </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> Income Tax Reference Application No.280 Of 2014  </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Borhanuddin, J.</p><p><b>Court:</b> High Court Division,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Mohammod Hossain, Advocate,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2019(1) LNJ </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2019</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Md. Elias  </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  The Commissioner of Taxes, Narayangonj  </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Income Tax Ordinance </p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2020-03-15</p><!DOCTYPE html><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">HIGH COURT DIVISION</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center; line-height: 150%;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 150%;">(SPECIAL STATUTORY JURISDICTION)</span></strong></p><table border="0" cellpadding="0" cellspacing="0" class="MsoNormalTable" style="margin-left: 5.4pt; border-collapse: collapse; height: 211px;" width="641"><tbody><tr style="mso-yfti-irow: 0; mso-yfti-firstrow: yes; mso-yfti-lastrow: yes;"><td style="width: 286.625px; padding: 0in 5.4pt;" valign="top"><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;"> </span></strong></p><p class="MsoHeading8" style="margin: 0in -1.4pt .0001pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif; font-style: normal; mso-bidi-font-style: italic;">Borhanuddin, J</span></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: center;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">And</strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold',serif;">Sardar Md. margin: 0in -1.1pt .0001pt 0in;"><a href="file:///H:/Issue_November_19(2)/Issue%20__November__19__ITRA%20_280%20of%2014__Borhanuddin__7.doc#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;
